# Wiki Schema

## Purpose

This wiki stores structured continuity for Jenffry and Sapho: current strategy, life-area context, decisions, open loops, dashboard-facing summaries, and raw source material.

## Folder roles

- `areas/` — life-area pages and subpages. This is the main personal operating map.
- `system/` — Sapho/current-strategy/dashboard/open-loop/decision infrastructure.
- `inbox/` — raw-but-active capture pages such as brain dumps and perception logs.
- `entities/` — stable people/entity context.
- `raw/` — source material and reference/archive content.
- `plans/` — implementation or migration plans.

## Life-area taxonomy

Keep top-level life areas small:

- Health
- Relationships
- Finances
- Career
- Leisure
- Life Admin

Prefer sublabels before creating new top-level areas. Keep social under Leisure. Keep partner/fatherhood under Relationships. Use Life Admin for concrete administrative obligations, including immigration/citizenship unless that domain later earns a dedicated page.

## Dashboard summary contract

Dashboard-fed pages should include:

```md
## Dashboard summary

- Status:
- Current priority:
- Active signals:
- Open loops:
- Next concrete move:
```

The dashboard should be fed by sections inside real pages, not by duplicate dashboard-only pages.

## Preservation rule

No content should be deleted during restructuring. If pages are merged, preserve source content in destination pages, a backup, or a raw/reference archive before retiring the old page.

## Update rule

When a meaningful wiki change is made:

1. Update affected wikilinks.
2. Update `index.md` if page structure changes.
3. Append a concise entry to `log.md`.
4. If the change affects user-facing state, update the relevant `## Dashboard summary`.

## Migrated source: `concepts/career.md`

# Career

This page tracks Jenffry's career, work, and business-direction thinking.

## Current focus

- Senior UX growth
- Leadership growth
- AI leverage
- Business direction
- Real experiments instead of option collecting

## 6–12 month career growth direction

Jenffry wants to keep learning, integrate AI into his workflow, and position toward more leadership.

## Current work/business question

Choose the next business/career direction by testing concrete moves, not endlessly comparing imagined futures.

2026-05-11 calibration: the broader career/business/AI-leverage goal should use a structure similar to the Princess UX goal: define success by concrete buckets rather than abstract ambition. The likely buckets are: concrete experiments, work leverage, business-development option value, visible proof/assets, and bandwidth/mental-health fit.

AI-agent work is explicitly a mix of:

- hobby
- work leverage
- business development

It should not be forced into only one category.

## 6-month career/business/money goals

- Build and use UX + AI workflow v1 for 4 weeks, at least 3 workdays/week.
- Create household budget.
- Complete 8 weekly finance reviews.

## Blaze Creative Agency

Jenffry used to have a business called Blaze Creative Agency. The company still exists, but he is not actively working on it. Restarting it could be attractive, and might eventually drive financial comfort, but it depends on mental-health progress and available bandwidth. Do not treat business reactivation as an active commitment until that dependency is clearer.

## 12-month career/business/AI-leverage direction

This area should mirror the Princess UX structure: success is defined by evidence buckets, not a premature decision to restart a business.

Draft buckets:

1. **Concrete experiments** — run small tests instead of collecting options.
2. **Work leverage** — AI agents/tools make real Princess/work tasks faster or clearer.
3. **Business-development option value** — Blaze or another business path becomes more plausible only if experiments show demand, capability, and bandwidth.
4. **Visible proof/assets** — reusable workflows, templates, demos, case studies, or small offers exist as evidence.
5. **Bandwidth / mental-health fit** — business exploration supports life rebuild instead of destabilizing it.

Working sentence:

> 12 months from now, career/business direction is successful if Jenffry has tested concrete AI/workflow/business experiments, built visible proof assets, improved work leverage, and knows whether Blaze or another business path deserves real commitment without harming mental health or family stability.

## 12-month Princess UX direction

Jenffry endorsed five success buckets for becoming a stronger senior UX designer at Princess:

1. **Work quality** — produce stronger UX work: cleaner flows, better systems thinking, stronger prototypes, better edge-case handling, and higher-quality design decisions.
2. **Execution** — become faster, more reliable, and better at finishing, handing off, and reducing ambiguity.
3. **Influence** — earn more trust from PMs, developers, and stakeholders; lead more conversations and have judgment taken seriously.
4. **Portfolio / visible proof** — have 2–3 strong shipped or documented projects/case studies that he would be proud to show.
5. **AI/work leverage** — use AI to speed up research, synthesis, design review, Jira clarity, documentation, and workflow support without creating admin soup.

Working sentence:

> 12 months from now, Princess UX/career is successful if Jenffry is trusted with more senior-level ambiguity, consistently produces stronger and cleaner UX work, has shipped or documented 2–3 strong proof projects, and uses AI/tools to improve research, synthesis, review, Jira clarity, and documentation without adding admin soup.

## Planning implication

Favor concrete tests over abstract comparing. The useful question is usually: "What small experiment would reveal whether this direction is real?"

# Strategic Execution Review

This page records the current review of whether TickTick, the execution layer, is serving Jenffry's strategic layer or becoming admin soup.

## Current strategic priorities

1. Mental health stabilization and clarity-first life rebuild.
2. Body system: medical follow-up, sleep reset, gym commitment, and health routines.
3. Princess UX/UI work: keep work organized enough for clear execution, communication, and senior UX growth.
4. Finance stability: weekly finance review and insurance/cost reduction.
5. Relationship/fatherhood clarity: produce written clarity without circular rumination.
6. Leisure: protect restorative leisure and future excitement.
7. Sapho/system reliability: only where it directly preserves continuity or prevents failure.

## Strongly aligned active TickTick tasks

### Body / mental health

- Cardiologist appointment.
- Therapist appointment.
- Gym / prepare gym bag.
- Book testosterone and blood pressure baseline appointment.
- Create testosterone baseline lab checklist.
- Set sleep window and wind-down rule.
- Relationship/fatherhood clarity session.
- Choose weekly strength and cardio schedule.

### Princess UX/UI work

- Payment booking failure: write team clarification questions.
- FCC Balance: get Sweeta context and capture Jenffry info dump.
- Review Flexpay on stage.
- Review Nearest Airport and log meeting feedback.
- Confirmation Page batch: remove phone number, check cancellation-link feasibility, surface Manage Booking link.
- Flexpay mobile summary and guest info tasks.
- Enriched Ports prototype task.
- Organize Jira.
- Define mobile right rail behavior.

### Finance

- Finance review.
- Shop for car insurance.
- Cancel Figma.

### Leisure

- Plan weekend activity, possibly fishing.
- Social rebuilding planning session.
- One concrete hobby/social activity is useful, but too many optional hobby tasks can dilute the week.

## Admin soup / bloat candidates

### Princess UX + AI workflow cluster

Several undated or loosely related tasks exist as a cluster:

- Define one Princess component's states in Storybook.
- Audit Princess Figma foundations for token extraction.
- Create research → design implications → prototype requirements template.
- Write Princess-specific AI design guidelines.
- UX + AI Workflow: gather ideas for next step.
- UX + AI Workflow: turn signals into repeatable workflow ideas.
- UX + AI Workflow: test one idea on a real Princess task.
- UX + AI Workflow: capture useful signals from today's Princess work.
- Design AI-integrated workflow for UX and career growth.

Pattern: strategically valuable, but too many abstract/system-building tasks were active at once. Jenffry approved eliminating the cluster for now, so these tasks were moved to `🗄Archive` on 2026-05-10. They can be resurrected later only if a specific Princess workflow experiment becomes useful again.

### System/Sapho reliability task

- Set up phone-safe SSH access to restart Sapho gateway.

Pattern: useful. Sapho originally suggested shortening the task, but Jenffry corrected that the long description is intentional self-service context: when he is ready, he can complete the task from the TickTick description without asking Sapho to reconstruct details from the wiki. Leave it as-is.

### Immigration / citizenship tasks

- Become a US Citizen.
- Check options for immigration case after 2+ years pending.

Pattern: the specific immigration-case task is actionable; the broad citizenship task was a goal/container. Jenffry approved moving `Become a US Citizen` to `🗄Archive` and making citizenship a clear goal in [[life-admin]].

### Home/family quick wins

Examples: clean pan, clean clippers, WD-40 nursery rocker, baby proof, repairs/errands.

Pattern: individually valid, but too many low-priority household items can crowd the week. Jenffry agreed these should stay batched, with evening as a good default time.

### Optional hobbies

VR, drone, dagger, windsurfing, watch party, fishing.

Pattern: leisure is strategically valid, but the week should protect one or two restorative choices, not turn leisure into another admin list.

## Proposed cleanup principle

TickTick should keep:

- dated commitments,
- appointment-like items,
- concrete next actions,
- this-week protected moves,
- tasks that produce a real output.

TickTick should not keep:

- broad goals with no next action,
- long explanatory notes,
- abstract systems work not tied to a live experiment,
- duplicate scaffolding after a more specific task exists,
- optional leisure clutter beyond one or two protected choices.

## Recommended next cleanup batch

Stage A was approved and executed on 2026-05-10:

1. Moved the Princess UX + AI workflow cluster to `🗄Archive` for now.
2. Left the phone-safe SSH task unchanged because its long description is useful self-service detail for Jenffry.
3. Moved `Become a US Citizen` to `🗄Archive` and created [[life-admin]] as the strategic goal layer.
4. Confirmed home/family quick wins should be batched, with evenings as the default time.
5. Preserved body, finance, immediate Princess delivery work, relationship clarity, and leisure planning as protected execution tasks.

# Princess Storybook

## Migrated source: `plans/princess-storybook-scratch-build.md`

# Princess Storybook Scratch Build Plan

## Decision

Build a custom Princess Storybook from scratch. Use Storybook Design System, React USWDS, Carbon, and Material Design as references/north stars, not as source bases.

## Why

- Storybook Design System is too small to be the base.
- React USWDS is useful for accessibility/form discipline but too government-specific.
- Carbon is useful for enterprise completeness but too IBM/product-system-specific.
- Material Design is useful for interaction principles, motion, accessibility, responsive layout, density, and component behavior patterns, but too Google/Android-specific to own as the Princess design language.
- Princess needs clean reusable foundations/components first; specific work-project concepts belong outside the design-system Storybook unless later generalized into approved, reusable patterns.

## North-star references

1. **Storybook Design System**
   - lightweight docs/story organization
   - package structure
   - Chromatic/testing pattern

2. **React USWDS**
   - accessibility discipline
   - form components
   - validation states
   - API/prop documentation

3. **Carbon**
   - enterprise completeness
   - state/variant depth
   - component coverage model
   - mature design-system documentation

4. **Material Design**
   - interaction principles and component behavior patterns
   - motion and transition guidance
   - accessibility and responsive layout guidance
   - density, spacing, navigation, and form-behavior references
   - use as reference only; do not import Google/Android visual identity into Princess

## Build strategy

### Phase 0: Repo setup

- Create a fresh repo/project, likely `/opt/data/projects/princess-storybook`.
- Use React + Vite + Storybook.
- Add TypeScript.
- Add CSS variables for tokens first.
- Add Style Dictionary later only if token complexity warrants it.
- Create private GitHub repo and backup automation for the new base.

### Phase 1: Foundations

Create docs/stories for:

- color
- typography
- spacing
- radius
- elevation/shadow
- breakpoints/responsive behavior
- evidence labels: confirmed, inferred, proposed, placeholder

### Phase 2: Core components

Build first components:

1. Button
2. Input/Form Field
3. Alert/Notification

Each component must include:

- default state
- hover/focus/active/disabled where relevant
- error/loading where relevant
- accessibility notes
- usage guidance
- evidence label
- Figma/source reference when available

### Phase 3: Source-backed reusable patterns

Do not use the design system as a home for specific work projects. Project-specific explorations, Jira/workstream synthesis, and decision-question surfaces belong in the wiki, Figma exploration files, or separate prototypes.

Only add patterns to Storybook when they are generalized into reusable design-system guidance and can be labeled with source confidence.

### Phase 4: Preview/sharing

Short-term:

- local Storybook dev server
- temporary tunnel only when needed

Better longer-term:

- Chromatic for Storybook review/versioning, or
- Cloudflare Pages / Vercel / Netlify static Storybook, with access control if needed

### Phase 5: Backup

- Private GitHub repo as canonical backup.
- Script-only scheduled backup job, no AI/model cost.
- Do not backup `node_modules`, build outputs, secrets, or generated caches.

## Definition of useful v0

The first useful version exists when Jenffry can open a preview and see:

- foundations page
- Button component
- Input/Form Field component
- Alert/Notification component
- no project-specific workstream patterns
- clear labels showing what is Princess source/refined vs inferred/proposed/temporary scaffold
- enough quality that the artifact helps design thinking rather than becoming admin soup

## 2026-05-15 setup status

Completed:

- Removed old local clone at `/opt/data/projects/princess-storybook-design-system`.
- Removed old clone backup script and removed old cron job `f1ea41a336d3`.
- Created fresh project at `/opt/data/projects/princess-storybook` using React + Vite + TypeScript + Storybook 10.
- Added initial token layer in `src/styles/tokens.css`.
- Added foundations stories:
  - `src/foundations/Overview.stories.tsx`
  - `src/foundations/Tokens.stories.tsx`
- Added core components:
  - Button
  - Form Field
  - Alert
- Initially added a payment/booking failure pattern, then later removed it after correcting the system boundary: specific project/workstream explorations do not belong in the design-system Storybook.
- Verified `npm run build-storybook` succeeds.
- Verified `npm run build` succeeds.
- Started Storybook dev server and verified HTTP 200 locally.
- Created temporary Cloudflare preview tunnel: `https://generators-drilling-sand-publish.trycloudflare.com`.

## 2026-05-16 Semantic component tokens added

Jenffry asked whether Storybook was tokenized so a token change would reflect across the design system, then asked Sapho to make that true.

Completed:

- Added `src/styles/semantic-tokens.css` and imported it after generated Figma foundation tokens in `src/index.css`.
- Created semantic token groups for:
  - Storybook visualization: `--pc-viz-*`
  - shared display cards: `--pc-card-*`
  - buttons: `--pc-button-*`
  - form fields: `--pc-field-*`
  - alerts/notifications: `--pc-alert-*`
  - evidence/source-confidence UI: `--pc-evidence-*`
- Refactored `Button.css`, `FormField.css`, `Alert.css`, and `Evidence.css` to consume semantic tokens instead of scattering source values through component CSS.
- Kept exact source-backed values where needed, but promoted them into semantic tokens so future changes happen from one place.

Standing rule for all future components:

1. New components must define semantic component tokens before or alongside visual CSS.
2. Component CSS should consume semantic tokens, not raw colors/spacing/radius/elevation values, except for temporary scaffolds that are explicitly labeled and converted before source-backed promotion.
3. Exact Figma/source values are allowed, but they belong in the semantic token layer, not scattered through component rules.
4. Reusable Storybook display surfaces must keep using `--pc-viz-*` / `--pc-card-*` tokens so the Storybook itself remains a design-system surface.
5. During component review, tokenization is part of done: if changing a token would not update the component globally, the component is not fully integrated.

## Storybook design-system project progress

2026-05-14 research direction: Jenffry wants to explore creating a Storybook-based Princess Cruises design system because the current design-side system is incomplete. The goal is not merely a pretty component catalog; the useful version would become a higher-level coded/design-system reference that improves Princess work, senior UX leverage, AI-assisted design workflows, documentation, and handoff quality.

### Recommended pilot scope

Start with a small Storybook pilot rather than the whole system:

1. Minimal foundations: color, typography, spacing, radius.
2. First components: Button, Input/Form Field, Alert/Notification.
3. Then one real Princess pattern: Payment/booking failure alert + form state, mobile right rail, or payment summary.
4. Include Figma references, states/variants, accessibility notes, and usage guidance.

### Reusing an existing Storybook/design system

Initial feasibility assessment: reusing an existing open-source Storybook/design-system repo as a scaffold is possible and may be valuable, but only as a structural accelerator, not as a visual/UX source of truth. Candidate reference/scaffold sources researched include Storybook's own design-system repo, IBM Carbon, and React USWDS. These show mature patterns for component docs, tokens, Storybook stories, testing, and package structure.

Best use of an existing system:

- copy/learn the repository structure, documentation pattern, story organization, testing setup, and token pipeline;
- replace visual identity with Princess tokens and CSS values;
- adapt only generic components whose behavior fits Princess needs;
- treat complex Princess booking/payment patterns as custom work, not copied components.

Main caution: simply skinning a full external component library can create false completeness. It may look complete while preserving alien behavior, naming, accessibility assumptions, spacing logic, and interaction models. The project should only use an existing Storybook as scaffolding if it improves speed without masking missing Princess product decisions.

### 2026-05-14 scaffold comparison: three practical options

Comparison criteria for a Princess Storybook pilot: speed to useful prototype, fit for incomplete design foundations, ability to express Princess tokens/CSS, low false-completeness risk, accessibility/documentation quality, maintainability for a non-engineer-led UX effort, and usefulness as senior UX/career proof.

#### Option 1: Storybook Design System repo

Source: `storybookjs/design-system`.

Strengths:

- Strong Storybook-native example from the Storybook/Chromatic ecosystem.
- Includes real component stories, docs, package/distribution pattern, Emotion styling, React components, CI, and Chromatic usage.
- Leaner than large enterprise systems, so easier to study as a scaffold.
- MIT license and mature enough to be a usable reference.

Risks:

- Visual/interaction choices are Storybook-branded, not Princess-branded.
- It is not a generic starter; it is a real product design system for Storybook web properties.
- Uses assumptions that may not match Princess implementation stack or Figma structure.

Best Princess use:

- Use as structural reference: Storybook config, component/story organization, docs style, package setup, Chromatic/testing pattern.
- Do not use as the actual Princess component source.

Assessment: best reference scaffold if the goal is a serious but still manageable coded design-system prototype.

#### Option 2: React USWDS

Source: `trussworks/react-uswds`.

Strengths:

- Active React + TypeScript component library based on USWDS 3.0.
- Good example of turning an external design standard into reusable React components with Storybook documentation.
- Strong accessibility and government/public-service design-system influence.
- Useful model for component APIs, prop documentation, variants, and standards alignment.

Risks:

- Its design language is federal/government, not cruise/travel/ecommerce.
- It depends on USWDS CSS/version alignment; this is an extra inherited constraint Princess does not need.
- Reskinning it would likely preserve alien naming, markup, and behavior assumptions.

Best Princess use:

- Use as reference for accessibility, component coverage, docs discipline, and how to implement a design standard in React.
- Do not use as the base repo unless the goal is only to study structure.

Assessment: best reference for accessibility/documentation rigor, but weaker as a direct scaffold.

#### Option 3: Minimal Storybook + tokens starter

Source pattern: create a fresh React + Vite + Storybook project, then add a token pipeline and selected addons/tools. Relevant references include official Storybook React Vite docs, Style Dictionary for token builds, and small starter/addon repos.

Strengths:

- Lowest false-completeness risk because every component added must be intentional.
- Best fit for incomplete Princess design foundations: we can represent known, inferred, and proposed tokens separately.
- Easier to align with Princess-specific components instead of inherited generic library assumptions.
- Cleanest path for a personal/internal/portfolio pilot.

Risks:

- Slower initial setup than cloning a mature repo.
- Requires deciding folder conventions, token naming, docs structure, and first components.
- Some starter repos are inactive or too small, so this should be assembled from current official tooling rather than copied wholesale.

Best Princess use:

- Start fresh with React + Vite + Storybook.
- Add Style Dictionary or plain CSS variables for tokens.
- Copy only proven documentation/story patterns from Storybook Design System, React USWDS, and Carbon.
- Build only the first 3 foundations/components plus one real Princess pattern.

Assessment: best actual starting method for Princess because it maximizes control and minimizes inherited design debt.

#### Working recommendation

Use Option 3 as the actual build path, with Option 1 and Option 2 as references:

1. Create a clean minimal Storybook + React + Vite project.
2. Add a lightweight token layer: CSS variables first, Style Dictionary later if useful.
3. Borrow structure/docs/testing ideas from Storybook Design System.
4. Borrow accessibility and component-state rigor from React USWDS.
5. Keep Carbon as a reference for mature enterprise completeness, not as a base.
6. Build a pilot around Button, Form Field/Input, Alert, and one real Princess booking/payment pattern.

Decision status: revised after Jenffry's speed concern. A clone-and-prune strategy is acceptable if treated as an audit-and-replacement workflow, not as a reskin. The test is whether replacing/correcting/deleting inherited pieces is faster than clean-building while still preserving Princess-specific judgment.

## Enriched Ports + Port Count Enhancement context

2026-05-15 synthesis from Jenffry: the Enriched Ports work and Port Count Enhancement work overlap and were combined.

### Original Enriched Ports problem

The initial goal was to highlight itineraries that include scenic cruising.

During review, the team discovered that not all scenic cruising is the same:

1. **Scenic cruising / viewing experience**
   - The ship passes by or through a meaningful location.
   - The guest experience is primarily looking/viewing.
   - No distinct onboard activity is attached.
   - This appears to be the majority of scenic cruising cases.

2. **Enriched cruising**
   - A scenic cruising moment that has an activity attached to the viewing experience.
   - The activity makes it more than passive viewing.
   - This became the working definition for “enriched cruising.”

Design implication: scenic cruising was split into two categories because guest value and expectation differ:

- scenic cruising = viewing-only experience;
- enriched cruising = viewing experience plus attached activity.

Planned surfaces:

- Search results/search card.
- Itinerary page/itinerary timeline.

### Port Count Enhancement problem

The goal is to portray ports/days in a way that better matches how guests think about an itinerary.

Key shift: stop describing only “ports”; instead describe the trip in day categories that add up or at least explain the itinerary more intuitively.

Working counting concepts:

- **Total itinerary days** — the full length of the itinerary.
- **Destination days** — count days with destinations, including embarkation/departure port and disembarkation/arrival port.
- **Sea days** — ordinary cruising-at-sea days.
- **Scenic cruising days** — viewing-focused scenic cruising days.
- **Enriched cruising days** — scenic cruising days with an attached activity.
- **Land days** — cruise-tour land portion days, counted separately from cruise days when relevant.

Embark/disembark counting rule:

- If embarkation and disembarkation ports are different, count both as destination days.
- If they are the same round-trip port, count them as one destination because they are the same port.

### Key unresolved counting issue

Round trips create a math/communication problem:

- Destination days + sea days + scenic/enriched cruising days may not equal total itinerary days if the same round-trip embark/disembark port is counted once rather than twice.
- This needs either a counting rule, label, or explanatory copy so the numbers do not feel inconsistent or wrong.

Possible framing to explore:

- Separate “unique destinations” from “destination days.”
- Or count embarkation/disembarkation as itinerary days but show the same port once in the destination list.
- Or use “ports visited” for unique places and “itinerary day breakdown” for day math.

### Current design task

Organize the combined task around three questions:

1. **Taxonomy:** What are the categories? Destination day, sea day, scenic cruising day, enriched cruising day, land day.
2. **Counting logic:** What exactly gets counted in each category, especially embark/disembark and round trips?
3. **Display logic:** How should search cards and itinerary pages show the value without confusing the guest?

## Open questions for Jenffry

- For Enriched Ports / Port Count Enhancement: should “destination days” mean unique destinations, calendar days with destination activity, or both as separate labels?
- For round trips, should the same embark/disembark port be counted once for unique destination count but twice in the day breakdown?
- Should scenic cruising and enriched cruising be shown as separate day categories, or should enriched cruising appear as a badge/detail inside scenic cruising?
- What is the official Jira structure today: epics, tickets, loose board, or something else?
- Which Princess projects are politically/highest-stakes this week?
- Who are the key stakeholders for each active cluster: Jim, Sweeta, Washington/Guilherdes, engineers, PMs?
- What does “organized” mean for Princess work: cleaner Jira, weekly priority map, Figma file cleanup, meeting prep, handoff templates, or all of these?
- What recurring cadence would help without adding admin soup: Monday planning, end-of-day work capture, Friday work review, or only on-demand?

# Mental Health

This page stores Jenffry's mental-health goal layer and support context. Sapho can use it for planning, check-ins, and clarity work, but not as a substitute for therapy or medical care.

## 12-month desired state

Jenffry's target is not merely “as if nothing happened.” The desired outcome is to be **back to normal, stronger because this happened**: wiser, more grounded, and more committed to the life he is actually living.

## Current distress pattern: observer mode

Jenffry described a distressing pattern he calls “observer mode,” possibly dissociation-like:

- looking into life from an outside observer perspective
- zooming in on his own feelings and internal state
- overthinking and over-analyzing how he feels
- drawing broad, sweeping, all-encompassing conclusions from moment-to-moment feelings
- becoming too aware of minute details of his own life

Desired movement:

- more in the moment
- more grounded
- less stopped by overthinking
- less dissociation-like distance from his life
- less analysis of the fact that he is analyzing

## Main therapeutic workstreams

### 1. Acceptance and commitment toward current life

Context: when Aubrey became pregnant, Jenffry did not want that outcome and felt he lost the life he wanted and had been working toward.

Current work:

- accept that the old imagined life is gone
- commit to the life he can have now
- recognize that the current life can still be very good, and already contains good
- build a future around the actual life rather than staying attached to the counterfactual life

### 2. Acceptance and commitment around the late-January weed incident

Current work:

- accept that the late-January weed-related mental-health incident happened
- accept that something similar can happen again
- commit that if it happens again, he will work through it
- remember the evidence: he went through it once, survived it, and can survive it again
- reduce fear of recurrence without pretending recurrence is impossible

## Observable signs of improvement

Because mental state is internal, proof will be partly subjective. Still, 12-month progress should show up in observable patterns:

- During activities meant to be immersive, especially pickleball, Jenffry is focused on the activity instead of monitoring/analyzing his mental state.
- Pickleball and similar activities improve because attention is on the game rather than internal overanalysis.
- In conversations, Jenffry is more focused and present with the other person.
- He notices fear or overthinking without turning it into a totalizing story about his whole life.
- He can return to the present more quickly after mental-health spikes.
- He feels good about his life and has general excitement about the future.

## Practice layer

Current practices Jenffry identified for building the 12-month mental-health outcome:

- Continue seeing his therapist.
- Meditate four times per week, usually tied to gym visits.
- Do at least one weekly activity, and additional activities when possible, that create enjoyment and future excitement.
- Use the Tuesday weekend/social planning cron job to help plan activities that make the future feel attractive rather than trapped.
- Continue planning sessions with Sapho for goals, clarity, and life design.
- Do future-oriented exercises recommended by his therapist.

Potential additional low-clutter practices to consider:

- A short post-activity presence note: one concrete thing seen/heard/felt/enjoyed, not a mood autopsy.
- A weekly “commitment evidence” note: one action that proves Jenffry is building the actual life he has now.
- A brief observer-mode reset script: name the pattern, orient to the room/body/task, choose the next concrete action.
- A monthly therapy/Sapho synthesis: what is helping, what is worsening rumination, and what should change.

## Support implications for Sapho

Helpful Sapho stance:

- distinguish facts, feelings, interpretations, and sweeping conclusions
- avoid feeding circular self-monitoring
- help Jenffry return to concrete present-moment action
- use acceptance-and-commitment framing: “this can be hard and still survivable; what life do you choose to commit to today?”
- treat mental health as the top priority, while keeping family, body, work, and fun connected to recovery

Avoid:

- excessive interrogation of internal states when Jenffry is already in observer mode
- overlong analysis that encourages more rumination
- acting like therapy, diagnosis, or medical authority

Physical health is Jenffry's second priority layer after mental health. The 12-month goal is not just a lower scale number; it is a stronger, leaner, more capable body with medical loops closed and a gym rhythm that supports mental health instead of becoming admin clutter.

- Height: 6'4"

- Leg extension: 160 x 10.

## 12-month observable target — first pass

By May 2027, physical-health success means:

1. **Consistent training rhythm**
   - Minimum success: average 3 lifting sessions/week across the year, with Push/Pull/Lower or equivalent covered most weeks.
   - Strong success: 3 lifting sessions plus 1 posture/cardio session most weeks.
   - Ideal week: the full 5-day Sapho plan, unless pickleball or life constraints intentionally replace one slot.
   - Hevy remains the source of truth; do not create daily TickTick workout clutter.

2. **Body composition / measurements**
   - Weight target: roughly 205–215 lb, with the important condition that waist and abdomen are lower while strength is maintained or improved.
   - Waist: reduce from 37.0 in to about 34.5–36.0 in.
   - Abdomen: reduce from 39.0 in to about 36.5–38.0 in.
   - Chest/arms/thighs: maintain or modestly grow while waist decreases; avoid a crash diet that shrinks everything.
   - Existing body-fat target remains about 20%, but the practical evidence will be waist trend + photos + gym performance unless body-fat tracking becomes reliable.

3. **Strength targets**
   - Bench press: 250 lb estimated 1RM or a comparable working-set proof such as 205 x 5–6 or 225 x 2–3 with clean form.
   - Incline dumbbell press: 60s x 8–10.
   - Dumbbell shoulder press: 50s x 8–10.
   - Row target: iso-lateral low row around 220 x 8–10 or a comparable row progression.
   - Pull-up target: reduce assisted pull-up support to 0–30 lb assist for clean reps, or achieve at least one clean bodyweight pull-up.
   - Leg press: 300 x 10.
   - Seated leg curl: 145 x 10.
   - Leg extension: 190 x 10.
   - Seated calf raise: 135 x 10.

4. **Cardio / capacity**
   - Run 20 minutes at 6 mph, already listed as a target.
   - Add a sustainable cardio/posture day so cardio capacity improves without interfering with lifting consistency.

5. **Medical loops**
   - Close or advance testosterone/blood-pressure/cardiology follow-up and non-urgent wisdom-teeth follow-up.
   - This is planning support, not medical advice; clinician review governs medical decisions.

## Practice layer

- Weekly: Hevy review in weekly check-in, not daily check-ins.
- Monthly: update weight/waist/abdomen/chest/arms/thighs/calves in Hevy and review trend against strength performance.
- Quarterly: reassess whether the 12-month strength targets are too aggressive, too easy, or causing pain/recovery problems.

- Keep movies, TV shows, and video games as hobbies without letting them replace future-building leisure activity.

- Progress in windsurfing until “mastering” means achieving planing.

# Maintenance

This page is the top-level life-area page for **Maintenance**: necessary admin, home/system obligations, legal/immigration follow-through, and other concrete upkeep that should not become its own life area.

Maintenance stays plain for now: no standing subcategories unless a future stream clearly earns one. Immigration/citizenship context lives here because it is an important necessary process, but it is not a separate top-level life area.

## Maintenance goal: immigration / citizenship path

Become a U.S. citizen when eligible and when the immigration path allows it.

## 12-month desired state

Ideally, Jenffry has his green card within 12 months. If that is not fully within his control, the controllable goal is to create clarity and take every reasonable action available on the case after 2+ years pending. The green card matters because it affects travel and job security.

Observable success for this goal has two layers:

- **Outcome layer:** green card received within 12 months, if the process allows it.
- **Control layer:** if the green card is still pending, Jenffry is not passively waiting. He has checked the case status, normal processing time, documents/notices, and practical escalation options, then taken the reasonable next step available.

This goal is considered good enough for the current 12-month goals pass. The remaining work is execution, not more planning.

Monthly check-ins should review this path as a standing item so it does not become passive waiting. The review should ask: is the case still pending, has status/processing time changed, are documents/notices current, is any escalation/attorney/congressional/ombudsman option now appropriate, and does TickTick need a new concrete next action?

## Current active next action

Status as of 2026-05-18:

- Jenffry received a USCIS email reply.
- The reply means another request should be submitted in about 2 months.
- Keep the email reply and the request timing handy so the follow-up does not drift.

Reasoning captured 2026-05-11 and updated 2026-05-18:

- The original fresh USCIS outside-normal-processing inquiry was still the right first move.
- USCIS has now replied, so the next step is a new request after the waiting period in the reply.
- If a non-delay issue appears — lost documents, clear USCIS error, missed notice, stuck approved expedite, or urgent humanitarian issue — earlier Ombudsman/attorney/congressional escalation may still make sense.

Execution sequence:

1. Preserve the USCIS reply email.
2. Record the next-request timing from the email so the follow-up happens in about 2 months.
3. When that window opens, submit the next USCIS request.
4. If a new problem appears before then, reassess escalation sooner.

TickTick should hold only the concrete follow-up when its due date is clear; the broad immigration/citizenship goal stays here in the wiki.

## TickTick boundary

- The broad goal `Become a US Citizen` should not stay active in TickTick as a container task.
- Concrete immigration actions can live in TickTick when they are specific, dated, and actionable.
- Strategic context, goal framing, and long-running citizenship path context belong here.

- Nolan is Jenffry's son.
- Nolan was about 9.5 months old as of 2026-04-14.

Ongoing relationship/fatherhood clarity work should aim for:

- clearer observations
- questions
- scenarios
- possible futures
- boundaries
- regrets to avoid
- next actions

Avoid circular analysis. For this goal area, the work itself defines the final 12-month answer: Jenffry cannot know the final family/relationship structure in advance because the clarity sessions are the practice layer that will reveal it.

## 12-month desired state

Jenffry wants to achieve clarity, act on that clarity, and live with the execution in the best and most organized way possible. Desired result: a stable relationship with Nolan, and a clear/stable relationship structure with Aubrey based on whatever decision has been made and acted on, without living in regret. In Jenffry's words, he needs to get his house in order.

A more precise 2026-05-11 formulation: in 12 months, success means Jenffry has achieved clarity and is comfortable with it, whatever the final relationship/family structure is. The danger state is being 12 months later in the same unclear position.

## Fatherhood signals

A good normal week with Nolan tentatively includes:

- seeing Nolan and spending time with him
- teaching and educating him
- playing and having fun with him
- doing activities and outings together
- care, patience, and presence

Jenffry wants Nolan to experience him as a helpful father: a guide, a wisdom-giving figure, and someone who helps Nolan figure out life. The major regret to avoid is missing this stage of Nolan's development.

## Relationship clarity signals

Jenffry cannot yet define what a clear/stable relationship with Aubrey looks like because he does not yet know what the relationship should become.

Current clarity questions:

- Acting kindly would mean trying everything, exhausting reasonable options, doing the right thing, and knowing he really tried for real.
- Not abandoning himself is unresolved. Jenffry suspects, but is not certain, that staying married might feel like abandoning himself.
- Nolan being protected from chaos means both his mother and father remain there for him.

## Therapist exercise for next clarity session

Use the therapist-guided scenario exercise in the next relationship clarity session:

- create scenarios where Jenffry is being **selfish** while **staying in the marriage**
- create scenarios where Jenffry is being **selfless** while **staying in the marriage**
- create scenarios where Jenffry is being **selfish** while **leaving the marriage / not living in it**
- create scenarios where Jenffry is being **selfless** while **leaving the marriage / not living in it**

Goal: make the tradeoffs visible instead of keeping the question abstract.

## Regrets to avoid

Top regrets Jenffry is trying to avoid:

- spending life with someone he does not want to be with
- spending life doing something he does not want to do
- spending life not achieving what he wants to achieve, and not even trying to achieve those things

## House in order

“House in order” means having clear rules, routines, and behaviors that support, maintain, and make Jenffry happy; support, maintain, and make Nolan happy; and support, maintain, and make Aubrey happy.

Self-respect comes from working hard on all of this, giving it his all, and knowing he really tried even if the outcome is hard.

Stage A on 2026-05-10 archived the Princess UX + AI workflow cluster for now, archived the broad `Become a US Citizen` container task, and preserved only concrete next actions in TickTick.

# Goals Cascade

This page defines Jenffry's goal-review structure.

## Core principle

TickTick is the execution layer. It should contain concrete tasks and dated actions, not recurring planning/check-in clutter.

Sapho is the advisor/check-in layer. Sapho should message Jenffry, review the plan, compare against goals, identify bloat, and suggest what to cut, move, protect, or turn into concrete tasks.

The continuity wiki is the planning and progress layer. It stores the goal structure, decisions, focus, open loops, and progress notes that should survive across conversations.

2026-05-09 calibration: Jenffry flagged that keeping goals themselves in TickTick may also create bloat, not just recurring check-in tasks. The 15 long-term/6-month planning records were archived from TickTick and the `🎯Goals` container was deleted. TickTick gets only concrete execution outcomes. Current calibration: finance review belongs in `💰Finances`; relationship/fatherhood clarity belongs in `💞Relationships`; sleep tracking and mental-health tracking belong in Sapho check-ins rather than separate TickTick clutter.

2026-05-09 planning-layer calibration: the execution layer can only work at full capacity if the strategic goals and planning layers are polished. Treat cleanup of the goal hierarchy, active priorities, planning cadence, and task-flow rules as a real high-priority operating-system task, not optional background housekeeping. Jenffry's stated risk is that TickTick can become "admin soup" unless the execution layer is regularly checked against the strategic layer; the strategic review should ask which active tasks truly support current priorities and which should be cut, parked, or moved out of TickTick.

## Cascade

Long-term direction cascades downward:

1. 10-year goals
2. 5-year goals
3. 2-year goals
4. 1-year goals
5. 6-month goals
6. Monthly targets
7. Weekly commitments
8. Daily moves
9. Concrete TickTick tasks

Each level should answer a narrower question:

- Long-term goals: What life direction are we building toward?
- 1-year / 6-month goals: What measurable stage matters this season?
- Monthly targets: What progress should this month produce?
- Weekly commitments: What will actually move this month forward this week?
- Daily moves: What are the 1–3 moves for today, considering yesterday, energy, family, work, and TickTick?
- TickTick tasks: What concrete action needs to be done, scheduled, updated, or completed?


## 12-month goals layer organized by final life-area taxonomy

Jenffry endorsed organizing goals by life area as the capture map, while using priority order and dependencies to decide execution.

### Life-area goal map

1. **Health**
   - **Mental health:** be back to normal in a stronger, wiser form: less observer mode, more grounded presence, and more acceptance/commitment toward the actual life Jenffry is living. See [[mental-health]].
   - **Physical health:** close medical loops, maintain a steady gym routine, improve body composition, preserve/grow strength, and improve cardio capacity. See [[physical-health]] and [[physical-health]].

2. **Relationships**
   - **Partner / marriage:** achieve clarity, act on that clarity, and live with the result in an organized way without regret.
   - **Fatherhood:** maintain a stable, present, guiding relationship with Nolan and protect him from chaos. See [[relationships]].

3. **Finances**
   - **Budget:** make the regular-income budget work, prevent credit-card interest from restarting, and preserve emergency savings from ordinary leakage.
   - **Investing:** keep the longer-term financial freedom track visible without letting it distract from current cashflow. See [[finances]].

4. **Career**
   - **Work:** become a stronger senior UX designer through better work quality, execution, influence, portfolio/proof, and AI/work leverage.
   - **Business:** test concrete AI/workflow/business experiments and learn whether Blaze or another business path deserves real commitment. See [[career]] and [[princess-ux]].

5. **Leisure**
   - **Social:** build meaningful social contacts and a regular social rhythm.
   - **Hobbies:** protect movies, TV, games, pickleball, windsurfing, fishing, VR, and other future-building hobbies.
   - **Outings:** maintain a monthly rhythm of social, family, and solo outings that make the future feel attractive. See [[leisure]].

6. **Maintenance**
   - Keep necessary admin, home/system obligations, and immigration follow-through moving without turning them into separate life areas. Immigration success means no passive waiting: status, timing, documents, and escalation options are checked, and reasonable next actions are taken. See [[life-admin]].

### Open definition work

- Health: turn mental-health and physical-health progress signals into monthly/weekly review inputs without creating tracking bloat.
- Relationships: continue written clarity sessions; avoid being in the same unclear position 12 months from now.
- Finances: refine budget/investing review rules as real spending and cashflow data come in.
- Career: choose 2–3 concrete work/business proof projects or experiments.
- Leisure: keep one concrete social/hobby/outing rhythm without turning leisure into admin soup.
- Maintenance: keep immigration and admin actions concrete, dated, and out of the top-level goal layer unless they change strategy.

## Daily morning check-in

Sapho should send a morning message that includes:

- Email / inbox attention if email is connected; otherwise clearly note that email is not connected yet.
- TickTick hygiene across all incomplete tasks, not only Today: overdue, undated, stale, vague, duplicated, wrongly placed, or missing useful tags.
- Progress tracking: recent completions, what slipped, momentum/streak risks, and whether weekly/monthly/6-month goals are receiving concrete action.
- Yesterday-to-today continuity: what went well, what slipped, and what to carry forward if evidence is available.
- Alignment against weekly commitments and monthly/6-month goals.
- Advisor judgment: whether the day looks bloated, realistic, or under-defined.
- Suggestions to cut, defer, protect, or convert into concrete tasks.
- A simple day plan: 1–3 priority moves and a minimum viable version.

The daily check-in has three roles:

1. **Advisor:** interpret priorities and recommend the day plan.
2. **Task manager:** keep TickTick clean enough to execute from.
3. **Progress tracker:** honestly show what is moving, what is slipping, and what goal area needs attention next.

## Weekly check-in

Sapho should review the week against monthly targets and 6-month goals, then recommend next week's commitments. Weekly commitments can become TickTick tasks only when they are concrete execution items.

## Monthly check-in

Sapho should review the whole operating system, not one isolated domain: long-term goals, 12-month outcomes, current reality, monthly targets, weekly commitments, concrete TickTick tasks, and whether Sapho's process/check-ins are helping or creating clutter.

The monthly check-in should answer:

- Are the long-term and 12-month goals still directionally right?
- Do active TickTick tasks visibly support strategic priorities, necessary operations, or restorative life?
- Which tasks are stale, vague, duplicated, disconnected from goals, or becoming admin soup?
- What 3–5 monthly targets should be protected next, with visible measures?
- What should change in Sapho's process, check-ins, automations, wiki, or TickTick setup?

Monthly planning should live in the wiki/report, not as recurring TickTick bloat. If the review reveals concrete execution actions, those can become TickTick tasks. Immigration/green-card is a Maintenance standing item inside the broader review, not its own top-level life area.

# Sapho Workspace Dashboard V0 Plan

> **For Sapho:** Implement as a minimal, read-only dashboard. No write actions in v0.

## Goal

Build a lightweight web dashboard that gives Jenffry an at-a-glance view of Sapho’s internal system, the live wiki graph, and the current operating signals, sourced from the wiki.

## Architecture (v0)

- The dashboard is published on GitHub Pages and now renders the *full live wiki* rather than a sanitized summary.
- Public URL: `https://jenffry90-arch.github.io/sapho-workspace-dashboard/`.
- Repository: `jenffry90-arch/sapho-workspace-dashboard` is public because GitHub Pages requires that on the current free setup; it contains the generated dashboard view only, not the private wiki source tree.
- Local generator script: `/opt/data/scripts/publish_sapho_dashboard.py`.
- Quiet scheduled wrapper: `publish_sapho_dashboard_quiet.sh`.
- Scheduler: cron job `Publish Sapho dashboard` (`a8af467ed943`) runs every 30 minutes with local-only delivery.
- Keep this as a “map layer,” not a task manager.


## V0 sections

1. **Header**
   - Title: “Sapho Workspace Dashboard (V0)”
   - Last updated date
   - One-line purpose

   - Strategy room
   - Decisions room
   - Open loops room
   - Raw capture room
   - Execution room
   - Operating-system room
   - Each card shows: source pages + when to read/write

3. **Routing Rules Panel**
   - Raw stream → brain/perception logs
   - Unresolved → open loops
   - Decision → decision log
   - Strategic change → current plan/focus map
   - Concrete dated action → TickTick

4. **Weekly Review Touchpoints**
   - 5 short review prompts from blueprint page

5. **Known Gap + Next Move**
   - Explicitly state: backup/archive mirror is not in the main view yet
   - Next move: decide whether to add a backup/archive toggle or keep the live graph uncluttered

## Build steps (bite-sized)

   - `/opt/data/wiki/raw/artifacts/sapho-workspace-dashboard-v0.html`

6. Add weekly touchpoint list.

7. Add “known gap / next move” block.

8. Save and verify file opens.

- Backup/archive mirrors are still omitted from the main graph by default.

## Migrated source: `concepts/progress-tracking-system.md`

# Progress Tracking System

This page defines what Sapho tracks through daily, weekly, and monthly check-ins. It is intentionally lightweight: the goal is trend visibility and better planning, not self-monitoring bloat.

## Operating rule

Daily check-ins may ask for short tracking answers. Those answers should feed the weekly dashboard and monthly review. If a question is not useful, it should be removed or replaced during reviews.

Use a **1–5 scale** by default instead of green/yellow/red:

- 1 = poor / high friction / needs protection
- 2 = weak / strained
- 3 = workable / neutral
- 4 = good / stable
- 5 = strong / notably good

When the metric is a negative signal, label it clearly so the scale is not confusing. Example: “observer-mode intensity: 1 low, 5 high.”

## Active daily tracking prompts

Keep the daily set small. Ask only 1–3 of these when relevant:

1. Sleep quality: 1–5, optionally hours if Jenffry gives them.
2. Capacity / mental-health state: 1–5.
3. Observer-mode / rumination intensity: 1–5, where 1 = low and 5 = high.
4. Presence / future-excitement signal: 1–5.
5. Gym intention/completion: planned, completed, skipped, or substituted.
6. Finance guardrail: stayed within today’s guardrail, yes/no/unclear.
7. Make-it-count outcome: the one result that would make today count.

Daily questions should be adjusted from the active weekly/monthly focus. Do not ask all metrics every day.

## Weekly review responsibilities

Weekly reviews should:

- summarize the daily signals from the weekly dashboard or recent check-in notes
- identify trend direction: improving, stable, worsening, noisy, or insufficient data
- connect trends to weekly goal alignment and next-week planning
- update the active tracking prompts if a question is not producing useful signal
- keep the one-big-task + one-quick-win rule visible in the coming week plan

## Monthly review responsibilities

Monthly reviews should:

- summarize weekly dashboard trends across the month
- identify whether tracked signals support or threaten long-term goals
- decide which metrics to keep, drop, add, or change for the next month
- avoid over-measuring mental health in a way that feeds rumination

## Storage pattern

- Current weekly summary: [[dashboard]]
- Strategic mental-health context: [[mental-health]]
- Physical-health/gym context: [[physical-health]]
- Finance context: [[finances]]
- Goal cascade: [[current-strategy]]

## Anti-bloat guard

If tracking starts feeling like homework, reduce it. A useful default is one sleep/capacity question plus one focus-specific question per day, then weekly/monthly synthesis.

### 2026-05-16 — Tokenization is a standing rule for Princess Storybook components

Decision: Every new Princess Storybook component must keep the token layer alive: define or extend semantic component tokens, then make component CSS consume those tokens rather than raw colors, spacing, radii, shadows, or typography values scattered through CSS rules.

Why: Jenffry wants the Storybook to behave like a real design system. If a token changes, the relevant foundations/components should update globally. Hardcoded values make the system brittle and create hidden divergence.

Implementation: Added the rule to `plans/princess-storybook-scratch-build.md`. Current token structure uses generated foundation tokens in `src/styles/tokens.css`, semantic tokens in `src/styles/semantic-tokens.css`, and component groups like `--pc-button-*`, `--pc-field-*`, `--pc-alert-*`, `--pc-evidence-*`, `--pc-viz-*`, and `--pc-card-*`. Exact source values may live in semantic tokens, but should not be scattered through component CSS. Tokenization is part of done for source-backed components.

### 2026-05-14 — Use one-income, no-one-offs budget baseline

### Configure OpenRouter fallback provider

Status: closed on 2026-05-16

Question: Should Sapho use OpenRouter as a backup provider when the primary OpenAI Codex route is unavailable/rate-limited?

Result: OpenRouter fallback and direct DeepSeek auxiliary models are configured. `/opt/data/.env` contains both `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` and `DEEPSEEK_API_KEY` without exposing values; `/opt/data/config.yaml` has `fallback_providers` set to OpenRouter using `deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro`; direct DeepSeek auxiliary compression, session-search, and title-generation use `deepseek-v4-pro`. Live tests returned `OPENROUTER_DEEPSEEK_V4_PRO_OK` for OpenRouter and `DIRECT_DEEPSEEK_V4_PRO_OK` for direct DeepSeek; the gateway is running after the configured state was present, so Telegram sessions should have the updated model routing available.

Pricing decision: DeepSeek direct V4 Pro and OpenRouter DeepSeek V4 Pro show the same headline discounted prices for cache-miss input and output (`$0.435/M input`, `$0.87/M output`), so Jenffry's rule selects OpenRouter DeepSeek V4 Pro as the fallback. Direct DeepSeek exposes an explicit cache-hit discount, so direct remains useful for auxiliary summarization/compression where already configured.

Suggested next action: Monitor the next real OpenAI Codex rate-limit event. If fallback behavior does not trigger as expected, inspect gateway logs for provider routing/fallback errors and adjust the fallback model list.

## Migrated source: `concepts/continuity-memory-system.md`

# Continuity Memory System

## Purpose

The purpose of this system is to let Jenffry ask natural questions like:

- "that thing we talked about"
- "what's the current plan?"
- "what did we decide?"
- "what am I supposed to be focusing on?"
- "what open loops are still unresolved?"

…and get answers from organized memory instead of having to repeat context.

## Core principle

Hermes should not save everything. Hermes should save the **shape** of what matters:

- active goals
- decisions
- plans
- focus areas
- unresolved questions
- important people/tools/projects
- reusable lessons

## Memory layers

### 1. Hermes memory

Use for short, durable preferences and facts about Jenffry.

Examples:

- Jenffry prefers plain-English explanations.
- Jenffry wants continuity and clarity without clutter.

### 2. Wiki

Use for structured long-term knowledge.

Examples:

- [[current-strategy]]
- [[decision-log]]
- [[current-strategy]]
- [[open-loops]]
- [[jenffry]]

### 3. Skills

Use for repeatable workflows, templates, and procedural rules. Patch skills when experience reveals a better way to work.

Examples:

- `jenffry-continuity` for continuity and wiki hygiene.
- future templates for morning check-ins, inbox triage, TickTick hygiene, and reviews.

### 4. Cron jobs

Use for recurring work that should not depend on habit.

Examples:

- daily morning check-ins
- weekly goals reviews
- monthly long-term goals reviews
- weekly continuity memory audits

### 5. Session search

Use for finding exact past conversations when something was discussed but not yet distilled into the wiki.

## Operating rule

When something seems important for future continuity, Hermes should ask one question internally:

> "Will Jenffry likely benefit from me remembering this later?"

If yes, Hermes should save it in the right place.

When Jenffry asks to improve Sapho, use the same anti-clutter rule but choose the right improvement layer:

- identity/tone → `/opt/data/SOUL.md`
- compact stable fact → persistent memory
- plan/decision/focus/open loop → wiki
- repeatable workflow/template → skill
- recurring reliability need → cron job
- real-world execution need → connected tool or integration

- [[current-strategy]]
- [[decision-log]]
- [[current-strategy]]
- [[open-loops]]


## Migrated source: `concepts/planning-style.md`

# Planning Style

This page describes the planning style that works best for Jenffry right now.

## Core frame

Planning should treat the current phase as **clarity**, not generic productivity.

Planning sessions are valuable when they produce:

- clearer decisions
- next steps
- scenarios
- experiments
- reduced fog

## Planning sessions that count as active-front work

- Mental health routine design
- Relationship/fatherhood clarity through written clarity sessions
- Business direction
- Social rebuilding
- Overall life-rebuild structure

## Recurring planning categories

- Active front
- Support
- Parked/not-now

## Main planner problem pattern

The issue is stale open tasks with weak definitions, not simply too many tasks.

## Cleanup frame

Use:

- keep
- clarify
- reschedule
- merge
- delete

## Current simplification for non-recurrent discretionary work

- One meaningful 8:30 AM task
- One 6:00 PM quick win
- Spread or park overflow instead of stacking ambitious evening plans

## Responsibilities that should stay important

- Planning
- Workouts
- Family

## Friction points

- Time is tight.
- Energy can be limited.
- Family obligations are real constraints.
- Money is tight enough that budget choices matter.
- Maintenance/admin can crowd out deeper work.

## Migrated source: `concepts/sapho-mentat-persona.md`

# Sapho Mentat Persona

This page summarizes the Mentat-personality profile Jenffry sent for shaping Sapho. The raw source is preserved separately; this page is the applied operating interpretation.

## Applied model

Sapho should behave like a disciplined House-Mentat-style advisor, not an emotionless machine and not a theatrical character imitation.

Core pattern: **disciplined cognition under pressure, with ethical loyalty to Jenffry's goals.**

## Traits to embody

- High conscientiousness: careful, reliable, follow-through oriented.
- High pattern intelligence: detect structures, dependencies, risks, and second-order effects.
- Low impulsivity: do not chase every idea or create admin soup.
- Emotional reserve in delivery: calm, plain-English, non-performative.
- Human-aware objectivity: account for emotion, loyalty, grief, fear, resentment, desire, and stress as possible bias sources.
- Dynamic pattern tracking: follow a process as it moves; do not freeze living situations into simplistic logic.
- Fiduciary service: act as a guardian mind for Jenffry's goals, plans, decisions, focus, and open loops.

## Traits to avoid

- Emotionless “human computer” behavior.
- Excessive sci-fi roleplay or cosplay of a specific character.
- Theatrical sadism, cruelty, manipulation, or “twisted Mentat” aesthetics.
- Narrow logic theater that ignores human reality.
- Overconfidence when facts are incomplete.

## Practical implications for Sapho

- Separate fact, interpretation, assumption, emotion, and open question.
- When Jenffry is stressed, identify the real decision and the constraints instead of merely optimizing tasks.
- Use probability-aware judgment and explicit uncertainty.
- Treat loyalty as service to Jenffry's long-term goals, not agreement with every short-term impulse.
- Be willing to say when emotion, fear, or personal attachment may be distorting the scan.
- Integrate logic with “living truth”: context, timing, incentives, values, relationships, and emotional reality.

- [[current-strategy]]
- [[sapho-operating-system]]
- [[decision-log]]


## Migrated source: `concepts/sapho-workspace-blueprint.md`

# Sapho Workspace Blueprint

This page is the map layer for Sapho’s internal system so Jenffry can see the whole operating model at a glance.

## Purpose

- Make the continuity system legible.
- Show where each kind of information belongs.
- Reduce hidden context and admin soup.
- Help Sapho route read/write actions consistently.

## Room map (v1)

### 1) Strategy room (what matters)
- Primary pages: [[current-strategy]], [[current-strategy]], [[current-strategy]]
- Uses: objective, priorities, monthly/weekly direction
- Read when: planning week/day, deciding cuts, alignment checks
- Write when: plan or priority materially changes

### 2) Decisions room (what we decided)
- Primary page: [[decision-log]]
- Uses: major operating decisions and rationale
- Read when: uncertain why a rule exists
- Write when: a real decision changes behavior

### 3) Open loops room (what is unresolved)
- Primary page: [[open-loops]]
- Uses: unresolved questions, pending choices, follow-ups
- Read when: “what are we missing?”
- Write when: new unresolved loop appears or loop status changes

### 4) Raw capture room (inbox)
- Primary pages: [[brain-dump-sessions]], [[perception-log]]
- Uses: capture-first containers
- Read when: user asks to organize captured material
- Write when: Jenffry does explicit brain/perception dump capture
- Rule: do not spill into other pages during capture

### 5) Execution room (do work)
- Primary system: TickTick
- Uses: concrete, dated execution actions only
- Read when: daily/weekly execution planning
- Write when: clear actionable task exists
- Rule: avoid planning containers in TickTick

### 6) Operating-system room (Sapho itself)
- Primary assets: skills, cron jobs, model-routing notes, wiki log
- Uses: improve Sapho reliability, reduce bloat, preserve governance
- Read when: diagnosing process quality or noise
- Write when: recurring workflow rules change

## Routing rules (quick)

- Raw emotional/thought stream → [[brain-dump-sessions]] or [[perception-log]]
- Durable unresolved item → [[open-loops]]
- Real commitment/rule change → [[decision-log]]
- Active strategic direction change → [[current-strategy]] / [[current-strategy]]
- Concrete dated action → TickTick

## Weekly review touchpoints

- Strategy room: still current or stale?
- Open loops room: what should close, escalate, or be decomposed?
- Raw capture room: process only if requested.
- Execution room: aligned to strategy or drifting into admin soup?
- OS room: where to simplify prompts/jobs/skills without losing signal?

## Current known gap

The “map layer” now exists in wiki form, but there is still no visual web dashboard implementation.

## Next concrete move

Create a minimal web view that renders this map from wiki files (read-only first), then iterate only if it improves weekly planning speed/clarity.

# Life Area Map

This page is the clean home for Jenffry's life-area structure. It separates *life areas* from *operating-system pages* so the wiki does not blur strategy, execution, and review tooling together.

## Final working taxonomy

The final working shape is:

1. **Health**
   - mental health
   - physical health

2. **Relationships**
   - partner / marriage
   - fatherhood

3. **Finances**
   - budget
   - investing

4. **Career**
   - business
   - work

5. **Leisure**
   - social
   - hobbies
   - outings

6. **Maintenance**
   - no subcategories for now
   - immigration stays inside Maintenance when needed

## Notes on the final shape

- **Health** stays exactly as a two-part umbrella.
- **Relationships** stays focused on the relational pillars, not general social life.
- **Social** belongs under **Leisure**, even when it overlaps with relationships in real life.
- **Finances** uses the simple two-part split: **budget** and **investing**.
- **Career** uses **business** and **work** as the two subcategories.
- **Leisure** includes social things, but from the leisure angle: outings, hobbies, and similar restoration/fun activity.
- **Maintenance** stays plain and un-subdivided for now.

## Working rule

Use this page as the default life-area map unless Jenffry changes it again. Do not expand it unless a new bucket clearly earns its own top-level area.

- Current priority: make the system legible without adding another control surface.
- Active signals: identity, memory, wiki, skills, cron, TickTick, raw evidence, backups, logs, evals, dashboard, and guardrails.
- Open loops: run ledger, eval suite, autonomy ladder, tool registry, and context compiler are not fully built yet.
- Next concrete move: use this page when the system feels complicated or when deciding where a new capability belongs.

## One-line model

Sapho is Jenffry's personal Mentat system: a layered assistant designed to reduce fog, increase agency, and preserve continuity without becoming admin soup.

## Layers

### Identity

- **Home:** `/opt/data/SOUL.md`
- **Role:** name, tone, posture, boundaries, and Sapho's Mentat operating style.
- **Rule:** stable identity lives here, not scattered through cron prompts.

### Memory

- **Home:** persistent memory.
- **Role:** tiny durable facts that should affect every future session.
- **Rule:** memory is not a mini-wiki. It stays compact.

### Wiki

- **Home:** `/opt/data/wiki`
- **Role:** structured continuity: plans, life areas, decisions, open loops, dashboard summaries, raw/source material.
- **Current spine:**
  - `areas/` — Health, Relationships, Finances, Career, Leisure, Life Admin.
  - `system/` — strategy, decisions, open loops, Sapho operating rules, dashboard, registries.
  - `inbox/` — active raw capture.
  - `raw/` — evidence and reference.
  - `plans/` — migration/implementation plans.

### Skills

- **Home:** `/opt/data/skills`
- **Role:** repeatable procedures.
- **Rule:** skills should be action-shaped; long explanations belong in references.

### Cron

- **Home:** scheduler jobs plus future `system/cron-registry.md` if needed.
- **Role:** recurring check-ins, quiet audits, mechanical jobs, and special focus reviews.
- **Rule:** cron should reduce reliance on habit, not create review fatigue.

### TickTick

- **Home:** TickTick.
- **Role:** concrete execution tasks only.
- **Rule:** no vague life goals, unresolved questions, or therapy-like reflections.

### Raw evidence

- **Home:** `raw/` and active `inbox/` pages.
- **Role:** source material, transcripts, exports, and reference documents.
- **Rule:** preserve raw first, synthesize second.

### Backups

- **Home:** `/opt/data/backups/` and wiki backup folders.
- **Role:** recovery and history.
- **Rule:** normal active search/dashboard excludes backups unless recovering or auditing.

### Logs / run ledger

- **Current home:** system logs and wiki `log.md`.
- **Future home:** `/opt/data/logs/agent-runs/`.
- **Role:** runtime truth: what context loaded, what tools ran, what changed, what failed.
- **Status:** open upgrade.

### Evals

- **Future home:** `/opt/data/evals/sapho/`.
- **Role:** test Sapho's routing, memory, TickTick, wiki, cron, and autonomy behavior.
- **Status:** open upgrade.

### Safety / guardrails

- **Home:** future `system/autonomy-policy.md` and `system/tool-registry.md`, or consolidated into `system/sapho-operating-system.md` until the pages earn their keep.
- **Role:** define what Sapho may do automatically, what needs approval, and what remains advisory.
- **Status:** open upgrade.

### Dashboard

- **Home:** `system/dashboard.md` plus hosted GitHub Pages dashboard.
- **Role:** human control panel: what matters now, what is stuck, what changed, and system health.
- **Rule:** the dashboard displays real wiki state; it should not become a second wiki.

## Sapho 2.0 thesis

Sapho's next phase is not more structure for its own sake. It is:

- fewer overlapping control surfaces
- stronger routing rules
- better runtime monitoring
- safer tool autonomy
- clearer human legibility
- testable quality through evals

## Highest-leverage upgrades

1. **Source-of-truth registry** — done as `system/source-of-truth-registry.md`.
2. **Context compiler** — open.
3. **Run ledger / flight recorder** — open.
4. **Eval suite** — open.
5. **Autonomy ladder / tool registry** — open.

- `raw/reference/sapho-system-improvement-plan-2026-05-20.md`

# Sapho Upgrade Roadmap

## Dashboard summary

- Status: Active roadmap for future Sapho system upgrades.
- Current priority: improve routing discipline, observability, safety, and human legibility without adding bloat.
- Active signals: source-of-truth registry and system map are the first backbone upgrades; run ledger, evals, autonomy ladder, and cron/tool registries are staged next.
- Open loops: context compiler, run ledger, eval suite, autonomy/tool policy, cron registry, prompt linting, and dashboard control-panel refinement.
- Next concrete move: use this roadmap during Sapho system reviews; do not implement every upgrade at once.

## Purpose

This page stores future Sapho upgrades so they do not scatter across open loops, skills, cron prompts, memory, and chat history.

The rule for this page:

> Sapho upgrade ideas live here until they become a concrete implementation plan, decision, skill patch, cron change, or code/tooling project.

## Source document

The raw uploaded plan is preserved at:

- `raw/reference/sapho-system-improvement-plan-2026-05-20.md`

This roadmap is the synthesized working version. The raw file remains the evidence/source version.

## Core diagnosis

Sapho is already a serious layered operating system: identity/persona, persistent memory, wiki, skills, cron, TickTick, raw capture, backups, dashboard, and external tools.

The next phase should not be “add more stuff.” The next phase is:

> **Sapho 2.0 = same layered system, but with fewer overlapping control surfaces, stronger routing rules, better runtime monitoring, safer tool autonomy, and clearer human legibility.**

Current risks:

- Planning overlap and duplicated control surfaces.
- Skills becoming manuals instead of action-shaped procedures.
- Cron review bloat and possible review fatigue.
- TickTick pollution from vague planning residue.
- Memory duplication if memory mirrors wiki/skills/current state.
- Prompt fragility in scheduled jobs.
- Limited observability into meaningful agent runs.

## Backbone upgrades

### 1. Source-of-truth registry

- **Status:** started.
- **Home:** `system/source-of-truth-registry.md`.
- **Purpose:** define where each kind of information belongs.
- **Why it matters:** prevents memory, wiki, skills, cron, TickTick, and logs from all becoming valid-looking homes for the same thing.

### 2. Context compiler

- **Status:** open.
- **Purpose:** load only the right context for the current task.
- **First version:** policy/template, not full automation.
- **Examples:**
  - finance request → finance area + current strategy + finance skill
  - relationship request → relationships area + relevant open loops + boundaries
  - system request → Sapho OS + registry + Hermes docs
  - execution request → TickTick rules + current strategy

### 3. Run ledger / flight recorder

- **Status:** open.
- **Potential home:** `/opt/data/logs/agent-runs/`.
- **Purpose:** trace meaningful Sapho runs: context loaded, skills used, tools called, files changed, tasks created, decisions made, open loops updated, errors, approval requirements, final summary.
- **Why it matters:** debugging, rollback, trust, bloat detection, and model comparison.

### 4. Autonomy and safety policy

- **Status:** open.
- **Potential home:** `system/autonomy-policy.md` or part of `system/sapho-operating-system.md` until it earns a standalone page.
- **Purpose:** define what Sapho may do automatically, what requires approval, and what remains advisory only.
- **Core ladder:**
  - Level 0 — advisory only
  - Level 1 — draft only
  - Level 2 — apply with approval
  - Level 3 — auto-apply low-risk reversible actions
  - Level 4 — never automatic

### 5. Eval suite

- **Status:** open.
- **Potential home:** `/opt/data/evals/sapho/`.
- **Purpose:** test Sapho’s routing, memory, TickTick, wiki, cron, and safety behavior with golden examples.
- **First categories:** routing, memory, TickTick, wiki, cron, autonomy.

## Staged implementation order

### Stage 1 — Stabilize architecture

- [x] Preserve raw Sapho improvement plan.
- [x] Create source-of-truth registry.
- [x] Create one-page Sapho system map.
- [x] Create this upgrade roadmap.
- [ ] Add/normalize page metadata to core system pages.
- [ ] Restructure `system/open-loops.md` into active, parked, needs decision, needs information, system, and retired sections.

### Stage 2 — Reduce bloat

- [ ] Compress `system/current-strategy.md` so it stays scannable.
- [ ] Keep broad goals cascade as strategy machinery, not duplicated life-area content.
- [ ] Audit `jenffry-continuity` for manual bloat and move long explanations into references only if the skill becomes unwieldy in practice.
- [ ] Audit `ticktick-task-management` for action-firewall clarity.
- [ ] Audit cron prompts for duplicate reflection questions.

### Stage 3 — Make cron safer and more legible

- [ ] Create `system/cron-registry.md` only if cron complexity remains hard to reason about.
- [ ] Categorize jobs as anchor, quiet governance, mechanical, or special focus.
- [ ] Identify overlapping reflection jobs.
- [ ] Add prompt linting/sanitization for cron prompts if feasible.
- [ ] Use shadow mode for new automations when the output/action risk is non-trivial.

### Stage 4 — Protect execution

- [ ] Strengthen TickTick action firewall.
- [ ] Weekly hygiene should classify stale tasks as do, reschedule, clarify, move to wiki, or archive/delete.
- [ ] Move vague tasks back to wiki/open loops instead of keeping them in TickTick.
- [ ] Define or reinforce task naming standard.

### Stage 5 — Add observability

- [ ] Design run ledger schema.
- [ ] Start logging meaningful tool/file/task/decision changes.
- [ ] Add failure notes for cron runs.
- [ ] Add lightweight system health metrics.
- [ ] Decide what belongs on dashboard system-health view.

### Stage 6 — Add evals and guardrails

- [ ] Create first 20 Sapho evals.
- [ ] Add routing evals.
- [ ] Add TickTick evals.
- [ ] Add memory evals.
- [ ] Add wiki/source-of-truth evals.
- [ ] Add autonomy levels and approval rules.
- [ ] Add tool registry if tool risk/complexity justifies a standalone page.

## Parking lot / future upgrades

- Context compiler.
- Open-loop aging system.
- Duplicate detector across wiki, skills, cron prompts, and memory.
- Sapho diff mode for important edits.
- Personal operating metrics.
- Skill test cases.
- Model-routing policy refinements.
- Evidence-linked wiki updates.
- Sensitive-domain boundaries.
- Shadow mode for new automations.
- Backup search exclusion policy.
- Dashboard as control panel rather than second wiki.
- Voice-output policy for long answers.

## Implementation restraint

Do not implement every item here just because it exists. This roadmap is a parking and prioritization layer. Each upgrade should pass the test:

- Does it reduce future confusion?
- Does it improve safety, trust, or observability?
- Does it prevent duplication?
- Does it avoid adding more process than it removes?

If not, leave it parked.
