# Source of Truth Registry

## Dashboard summary

- Status: Active routing constitution for Sapho's information layers.
- Current priority: prevent duplication across memory, wiki, skills, cron, TickTick, and logs.
- Active signals: Sapho 2.0 should compress control surfaces, strengthen routing, and improve observability.
- Open loops: context compiler, run ledger, evals, autonomy ladder, and tool registry remain future upgrades.
- Next concrete move: use this registry before adding new pages, memories, skills, cron jobs, or TickTick tasks.

## Purpose

This registry defines the canonical home for each kind of information in Sapho. The rule is simple:

> Before saving or changing anything, ask: **what is the home of record for this?**

The goal is not to store less useful context. The goal is to stop the same context from living in five places where it slowly diverges.

## Routing table

### Identity, tone, and stable behavior

- **Canonical home:** `/opt/data/SOUL.md`
- **Also allowed:** compact persistent memory for high-value stable preferences; `system/sapho-operating-system.md` for structured explanation.
- **Not allowed:** TickTick, random cron prompts, duplicated skill manuals.

### Stable user preferences

- **Canonical home:** persistent memory.
- **Also allowed:** wiki only when the preference needs structured context or history.
- **Not allowed:** current plan pages, TickTick, raw logs as the only source.

### Durable plans and life context

- **Canonical home:** `/opt/data/wiki`.
- **Current structure:**
  - `system/current-strategy.md` for active strategy/focus/goals cascade.
  - `areas/` for life-area context.
  - `system/open-loops.md` for unresolved questions.
  - `system/decision-log.md` for decisions.
- **Not allowed:** persistent memory unless it is a tiny stable fact; TickTick unless it has a concrete next action.

### Active priorities and focus hierarchy

- **Canonical home:** `system/current-strategy.md`.
- **Not allowed:** duplicated independent focus pages or cron prompts as the only source.

### Decisions

- **Canonical home:** `system/decision-log.md`.
- **Format:** lightweight decision record: date, status, context, decision, rationale, consequences, links.
- **Not allowed:** memory unless the decision creates a stable preference; TickTick.

### Open unresolved questions

- **Canonical home:** `system/open-loops.md`.
- **Rule:** an open loop must eventually be promoted, parked, resolved, retired, or converted into a concrete next action.
- **Not allowed:** TickTick unless the next action is visible and executable.

### Repeatable procedures

- **Canonical home:** skills.
- **Rule:** skill body should be action-shaped; long explanation belongs in skill references.
- **Not allowed:** wiki planning pages as the only procedural source.

### Scheduled rhythms and recurring automation

- **Canonical home:** cron jobs plus `system/cron-registry.md` if/when created.
- **Also allowed:** `system/sapho-operating-system.md` for policy; `system/decision-log.md` for decisions.
- **Not allowed:** TickTick unless there is a user-facing action.

### Concrete execution tasks

- **Canonical home:** TickTick.
- **Admission rule:** a task needs a verb, object, clear done condition, life area, and a date only if timing matters.
- **Not allowed:** wiki, memory, or open loops as a substitute for executable tasks.

### Raw dumps and evidence

- **Canonical home:** `raw/` for source material, `inbox/` for active capture.
- **Examples:** `inbox/brain-dump-sessions.md`, `inbox/perception-log.md`, `raw/transcripts/`, `raw/reference/`.
- **Not allowed:** main planning pages without synthesis.

### Historical versions and backups

- **Canonical home:** `backups/` or `/opt/data/backups/`.
- **Rule:** normal active search excludes backups; recovery/audit search may include them.
- **Not allowed:** active dashboard/search scope unless explicitly requested.

### Runtime traces / flight recorder

- **Canonical home:** future `/opt/data/logs/agent-runs/`.
- **Not allowed:** decision log as a dumping ground for every tool call.
- **Status:** open upgrade.

### Test cases and evals

- **Canonical home:** future `/opt/data/evals/sapho/`.
- **Not allowed:** long test banks inside skill bodies.
- **Status:** open upgrade.

### Dashboard-facing state

- **Canonical home:** `## Dashboard summary` sections inside real wiki pages.
- **Not allowed:** a duplicate dashboard-only mini-wiki.

## Routing discipline

When new information arrives:

1. Identify the information type.
2. Route it to the canonical home.
3. If the canonical home changes, update this registry.
4. If the information is temporary, avoid persistent memory.
5. If the information is broad and unresolved, use open loops, not TickTick.
6. If the information is executable, use TickTick, not the wiki.
7. If the information is a procedure, use a skill.
8. If the information is evidence, preserve it under `raw/` before synthesis.

This registry was created from the uploaded Sapho System Improvement Plan, preserved at:

- `raw/reference/sapho-system-improvement-plan-2026-05-20.md`

# Brain Dump Sessions

This page is the collection point for Jenffry's freeform brain dump sessions.

When Jenffry explicitly says **"this is a brain dump session"** or clearly identifies a message as a brain dump, capture what follows here first, without prematurely organizing, judging, or turning it into tasks.

## Operating rule

- Preserve the raw thought stream in this page under a dated session heading while it is still unprocessed or pending Jenffry approval.
- Keep Jenffry's language and intent as intact as possible during capture.
- Do not over-summarize during capture.
- Do not add later-organization notes by default.
- Do not move content into other wiki pages or TickTick during capture.
- The brain dump page is the containment layer; processing happens later only if Jenffry explicitly asks to organize the dump.
- Every active session must carry a visible processing status so weekly reviews know what is new, reviewed, or awaiting action.
- Use these status values:
  - `raw/unprocessed` — captured but not reviewed yet.
  - `reviewed/proposed` — reviewed in place only; possible next actions noted, but nothing is moved unless Jenffry explicitly asks.
  - `partially processed` — reserved for when Jenffry explicitly requests organization and only some items are handled.
- Do **not** keep `processed` dumps on this page. Once Jenffry explicitly asks to process a dump and it is fully handled, delete that session block from this page so it does not create noise or consume context. The durable output should live in the destination wiki pages, TickTick if explicitly approved/requested, and the wiki log.
- Later, when Jenffry asks to organize the dump, sort material into the right places:
  - concrete execution items → TickTick, only if Jenffry explicitly approved or requested task creation
  - plans/decisions/focus/open loops → [[current-strategy]], [[decision-log]], [[current-strategy]], or [[open-loops]]
  - durable life/work context → relevant concept/entity pages
  - reusable ideas → appropriate wiki pages
- Avoid creating admin soup: this page is a temporary inbox for raw thought, not a permanent archive.

## Capture template

```markdown
## YYYY-MM-DD — Brain dump session

Status: `raw/unprocessed`
Reviewed on: _not yet_
Source: Telegram brain dump

### Raw dump

- ...
```

## Sessions

### 2026-05-18 — Brain dump session

Status: `partially processed`
Reviewed on: 2026-05-18
Processed on: 2026-05-18 (partial)
Source: Telegram brain dump
Action taken / destination links: created [[sapho-operating-system]] and updated [[open-loops]] for the dashboard item; remaining raw items still pending organization

### Raw dump

- Jenffry wants a dedicated social-life tracking stream, collected during the week and reviewed weekly, integrated with the rest of the planning system.
- He wants the wiki structure tightened so live areas each have a clear home page plus a collection/review space for raw improvement ideas.
- He wants the cleanup process to search specifically for items that fit the live-area structure rather than scavenging loosely.
- For relationship/fatherhood clarity, he wants to use a more direct, number- and data-oriented approach when useful.
- He remembers a prior hedonic-calculus / weighted-variable exercise and wants to use something like that again to gain perspective on staying versus leaving and the pain/benefit tradeoffs.
- He wants to get back to writing short stories and carve out dedicated time for that.
- He wants to restructure his mornings so there is protected time for planning, clarity, and thinking about the day before the gym routine consumes the whole morning.
- He feels the current morning flow is good for gym consistency, but it leaves too little room for mental clarity and day-shaping before the day fully starts.
- He wants to get back to clarifying and redesigning the goals layer, because unclear goals are hurting prioritization and making planning less effective.
- He wants a web dashboard that gives an at-a-glance view of all internal systems with Sapho.

# Perception Log

This page is a lightweight capture point for Jenffry's momentary inner-state dumps: emotions, body sensations, energy, stress, mood, pain/tension, clarity/fog, urges, random perceptions, and other felt signals.

The scope is intentionally broad. It is **not** only an emotions tracker. It is for “how I am experiencing myself right now,” including body and mind.

Like a brain dump, this page is a containment layer first: capture here now, process later, and avoid spilling the raw entry into other pages during capture.

Example triggers Jenffry might use:

- **"perception dump"**
- **"feelings dump"**
- **"body feeling dump"**
- **"log how I feel"**
- **"feeling check"**
- **"body check"**
- **"random perception"**
- any clear request to capture a current inner/body state

Sapho should append the entry here without over-analyzing in the moment.

This is not therapy, diagnosis, or medical assessment. It is a pattern-recognition layer: collect enough signal to notice repeated triggers, body-state correlations, helpful responses, danger states, and practical next moves.

## Operating rule

- Capture Jenffry's wording as directly as practical.
- Treat “feeling” broadly: emotional, bodily, cognitive, energetic, sensory, motivational, or hard-to-classify.
- Add light metadata only when available: date/time, context, body state, trigger, intensity, and immediate need.
- Do not force Jenffry to categorize the perception if the whole point is that it is vague or random.
- Do not turn every perception into a TickTick task.
- Do not over-refine entries in a way that feeds rumination or observer-mode self-monitoring.
- Weekly review should look for patterns, solutions, and insights; it should not pathologize or diagnose.
- After weekly review, keep this page lean: preserve patterns/insights here, and move reviewed raw entries into dated raw archive files only if they are becoming noisy.

## Quick capture template

```markdown
### YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM — Perception entry

- Raw words / perception:
- Type, if obvious: body, emotion, energy, thought, urge, sensory, mixed, unclear
- Context / trigger:
- Body state: sleep, food, caffeine, gym, illness, tension, pain, stomach, breathing, if known
- Intensity: 1–5 if naturally available
- Immediate need: vent, grounding, decision help, reassurance, action, rest, observe only, unclear
```

# Life Area Frameworks

This page captures common life-area models other people use, so Jenffry's own taxonomy can stay grounded in outside patterns instead of feeling invented from scratch.

## Common pattern across frameworks

Most life-area systems use **5 to 10 domains**.

They usually include some combination of:
- health
- work / career
- finances / money
- relationships / family / friends / partner
- personal growth / learning
- leisure / fun / recreation
- environment / home
- community / contribution
- spirituality / meaning

## Common models found

### 1. Wheel of Life

Commonly described as an **8 to 10 category** self-assessment or coaching wheel.

Typical categories include:
- Money & Finances
- Career & Work
- Health & Fitness
- Fun & Recreation
- Environment / home / work setting
- Community
- Family & Friends
- Partner & Love
- Personal Growth & Learning
- Spirituality

Sources:
- Positive Psychology: *The Wheel of Life: How to Apply It in Coaching*
- Scott Jeffrey: *Wheel of Life Assessment: 7‑Step Self‑Coaching Guide*

### 2. Five-domain life model

A simpler research-backed model often uses five domains:
- spirituality
- family
- work
- health
- community

This version is easier when the goal is to keep the taxonomy small.

Source:
- Positive Psychology: *What Are Life Domains & How Can We Balance Them?*

### 3. Self-care wheel style

A self-care version often splits life into:
- emotional
- spiritual
- personal
- professional
- physical

This is more of a self-care lens than a full life taxonomy, but it shows how some systems narrow the list when they want less clutter.

## What this means for Jenffry

Jenffry's current structure fits the common pattern well:

- **Health** maps to the health / physical / emotional cluster
- **Relationships** maps to family / partner / friends / fatherhood
- **Finances** maps to money / material wellbeing
- **Career** maps to work / productivity
- **Leisure** maps to fun / recreation
- **Maintenance** maps to environment / admin / necessary obligations

## Good rule from outside frameworks

Other people's systems usually do **not** try to force every life detail into a separate top-level area.

They usually:
- keep the total number of areas manageable
- adapt the names to the person's actual life
- allow subcategories or subdomains
- review the categories periodically rather than treating them as permanent truth

## Practical takeaway

Jenffry's current set is within the normal range of life-area models, and the sublabel approach for Relationships is consistent with how many wheel-of-life systems let a broad domain contain smaller subdomains.

Suggested next action: Complete the TickTick `Relationship/fatherhood clarity session`; use the new weekly Sapho clarity prompt to make the work recurring without turning the goal structure into TickTick bloat.

**Upgrade thesis**
raw/reference/sapho-system-improvement-plan-2026-05-20.md
degree 0

Below is the processed upgrade plan for Sapho as a personal Hermes AI agent system. The conversation shows that Sapho is already a serious layered operating system: SOUL/persona, persistent memory, wiki, skills, cron, TickTick, raw capture, backups, and extern

No resolved wikilinks.
Below is the processed upgrade plan for Sapho as a personal Hermes AI agent system.

The conversation shows that Sapho is already a serious layered operating system: **SOUL/persona**, **persistent memory**, **wiki**, **skills**, **cron**, **TickTick**, **raw capture**, **backups**, and external tools like Google Workspace and Hevy. The repeated critique across the conversation is not “Sapho lacks structure.” It is the opposite: Sapho is strong, but now needs **compression, routing discipline, observability, evals, guardrails, and better human legibility**.

## **Core diagnosis**

Sapho’s current architecture is good. The next phase should not be “add more stuff.” It should be:

**Sapho 2.0 \= same layered system, but with fewer overlapping control surfaces, stronger routing rules, better runtime monitoring, and safer tool autonomy.**

The system’s current risks are:

1. **Planning overlap**  
   `current-plan`, `focus-map`, `goals-cascade`, `life-rebuild`, `planning-style`, `open-loops`, and `decision-log` are all useful, but too close together.  
2. **Skills becoming manuals**  
   `jenffry-continuity`, `ticktick-task-management`, and `hermes-agent` are valuable, but risk becoming giant policy archives instead of clean procedures.  
3. **Cron review bloat**  
   The cron layer is useful, but many jobs touch reflection, planning, mental health, weekly review, perception review, and relationship clarity. That creates possible “review fatigue.”  
4. **TickTick task pollution**  
   TickTick is correctly the execution layer, but it can easily absorb vague planning residue, stale dated tasks, and unresolved life questions.  
5. **Memory duplication**  
   Memory is currently mostly healthy, but it must stay tiny. It should not mirror the wiki, skills, or current project state.  
6. **Prompt fragility**  
   Invisible Unicode or formatting issues already caused a cron failure, which means Sapho needs prompt linting/sanitization before scheduled jobs run.  
7. **Limited observability**  
   Sapho has logs and wiki history, but not a true “flight recorder” for agent runs: what context loaded, what tools were called, what decisions were made, what failed, and why.

Modern agent systems benefit from exactly these missing pieces: explicit orchestration/state ownership, tracing, guardrails, human review, and evals. OpenAI describes agents as applications that plan, call tools, collaborate across specialists, and maintain enough state for multi-step work; the SDK path is meant for systems that own orchestration, tool execution, approvals, and state. ([OpenAI Developers](https://developers.openai.com/api/docs/guides/agents))

---

# **Upgrade thesis**

Sapho should become a **lean personal agent operating system** with four new backbone capabilities:

1. **A source-of-truth registry**  
   Every kind of information has one canonical home.  
2. **A context compiler**  
   Sapho should load only the right context for the current task, not the whole system.  
3. **A run ledger / observability layer**  
   Every meaningful agent run should be traceable.  
4. **An autonomy and safety policy**  
   Sapho should know which actions it may perform automatically, which require approval, and which are advisory only.

This matters because context is finite. Anthropic’s context-engineering guidance frames agent reliability as a problem of curating the right state, tools, memory, external data, and history into the model context, not merely writing better prompts. ([Anthropic](https://www.anthropic.com/engineering/effective-context-engineering-for-ai-agents))

---

# **Phase 1: Create the Sapho source-of-truth registry**

Create one canonical registry file, probably:

`/opt/data/wiki/concepts/source-of-truth-registry.md`

Its job: define where each kind of information belongs.

## **Proposed registry**

| Information type | Canonical home | Not allowed in |
| ----- | ----- | ----- |
| Persona, tone, role | `SOUL.md` | Skills, cron prompts, TickTick |
| Stable user preferences | Persistent memory | Wiki unless detailed |
| Durable plans/context | Wiki | Memory, TickTick |
| Active priorities | `current-plan.md` | Random life-area pages |
| Focus hierarchy | `focus-map.md` or folded into `current-plan.md` | Cron prompts |
| Decisions | `decision-log.md` | Memory, TickTick |
| Open unresolved questions | `open-loops.md` | TickTick unless next-actionable |
| Repeatable procedures | Skills | Wiki planning pages |
| Scheduled rhythms | Cron | TickTick unless user-facing action |
| Concrete tasks | TickTick | Wiki, memory |
| Raw dumps/evidence | `raw/`, `brain-dump-sessions.md`, `perception-log.md` | Main planning pages |
| Historical versions | `backups/` | Active wiki search scope |
| Runtime traces | New `runs/` or `logs/agent-runs/` | Decision log |
| Test cases/evals | New `evals/` | Skills body |

## **Why this is priority one**

Right now, Sapho’s main bloat risk is not too much information. It is information living in too many valid-looking places.

This registry becomes the routing constitution.

Every future change asks:

**“What is the home of record for this?”**

---

# **Phase 2: Compress the planning layer**

The planning cluster is Sapho’s heaviest area.

Current cluster:

* `current-plan.md`  
* `focus-map.md`  
* `goals-cascade.md`  
* `life-rebuild.md`  
* `planning-style.md`  
* `open-loops.md`  
* `decision-log.md`

Do not delete them blindly. Instead, assign sharper jobs.

## **Recommended page roles**

### **1\. `current-plan.md` becomes the control tower**

It should be short and current.

Suggested sections:

\# Current Plan

\#\# Now  
The 1-3 active fronts.

\#\# Next  
The next few moves, not a huge backlog.

\#\# Waiting / Blocked  
Things not actionable yet.

\#\# This Week’s Operating Rule  
One behavioral rule for the current phase.

\#\# Links  
\- Focus map  
\- Open loops  
\- Goals cascade  
\- Decision log

Rule: if `current-plan.md` cannot be scanned in under two minutes, it is too heavy.

### **2\. `focus-map.md` becomes either a derived page or gets merged**

Current critique says `focus-map` and `current-plan` overlap heavily. Keep it only if it answers a different question.

Best distinction:

* `current-plan.md` \= what Sapho is helping with now  
* `focus-map.md` \= what should receive attention, energy, and protection

If that distinction does not stay useful, merge `focus-map` into `current-plan`.

### **3\. `goals-cascade.md` becomes a strict cascade only**

It should not become a philosophical planning page.

Keep only:

Long-term direction  
→ 12-month outcomes  
→ quarterly/monthly targets  
→ weekly commitments  
→ daily moves  
→ TickTick conversion rule

### **4\. `life-rebuild.md` becomes a high-level narrative**

This should not compete with current planning.

Its role:

* long-frame story  
* rebuilding principles  
* why the system exists  
* not active task steering

### **5\. `planning-style.md` becomes doctrine, not a plan**

Keep the core planning rules there:

* clarity-first  
* one meaningful task \+ one quick win  
* avoid ambitious evening stacking  
* planning only matters if it reduces fog

### **6\. `open-loops.md` gets split by status**

This page is carrying too much unresolved energy.

Recommended structure:

\# Open Loops

\#\# Active Open Loops  
Maximum 10\.

\#\# Parked / Later  
Valid, but not active.

\#\# Needs Decision  
Can be resolved by a choice.

\#\# Needs Information  
Cannot be resolved yet.

\#\# System Open Loops  
Sapho/Hermes architecture issues.

\#\# Retired  
Closed, stale, or deliberately dropped.

Rule: no open loop should live forever without being promoted, parked, resolved, or retired.

### **7\. `decision-log.md` becomes ADR-style**

Use a lightweight architecture decision record format:

\#\# YYYY-MM-DD — Decision title

Status: accepted / replaced / retired  
Context:  
Decision:  
Rationale:  
Consequences:  
Links:

This keeps decisions from turning into vague notes.

---

# **Phase 3: Add page metadata to the wiki**

Add small frontmatter to important wiki pages.

Example:

\---  
type: control-tower  
status: active  
home\_of\_record: current priorities  
last\_reviewed: 2026-05-19  
review\_cadence: weekly  
related:  
  \- open-loops  
  \- decision-log  
  \- goals-cascade  
\---

This makes the wiki easier for both humans and agents to route.

AWS’s RAG documentation emphasizes that clear headings and structure help retrieval systems understand and extract information from documents more effectively. Sapho’s wiki is effectively a personal RAG corpus, so page structure is not cosmetic; it directly improves retrieval quality. ([AWS Documentation](https://docs.aws.amazon.com/prescriptive-guidance/latest/writing-best-practices-rag/best-practices.html))

---

# **Phase 4: Refactor skills into lean procedures**

Current issue: some skills are drifting into operating manuals.

New rule:

**A skill should be action-shaped. A reference file can be explanation-shaped.**

## **Recommended skill structure**

Each major skill should have:

\# Skill name

\#\# Purpose  
One paragraph.

\#\# When to use  
Clear triggers.

\#\# Inputs needed  
What Sapho must know before acting.

\#\# Procedure  
Step-by-step method.

\#\# Output format  
What the answer/action should produce.

\#\# Boundaries  
What not to do.

\#\# References  
Links to deeper docs.

## **Compression targets**

### **`jenffry-continuity`**

Keep as the continuity governor, but slim the core skill.

Move long explanations into references:

* memory-vs-wiki.md  
* open-loop-policy.md  
* wiki-routing-policy.md  
* decision-log-policy.md

### **`ticktick-task-management`**

Split into:

* core task-routing skill  
* task hygiene reference  
* recurring review reference  
* TickTick API/troubleshooting reference

The skill body should mostly answer:

**“Is this a task, and how should it be represented?”**

### **`hermes-agent`**

This should probably stop pretending to be a normal skill.

Better role:

**Hermes platform handbook**

It can still be invoked, but it should be treated as system documentation for:

* CLI  
* cron  
* config  
* tools  
* MCP  
* model routing  
* backups  
* troubleshooting

### **Narrow skills**

Keep these narrow:

* `health-and-fitness-planning`  
* `personal-finance-budgeting`  
* `weekend-social-planning`  
* `google-workspace`

They are closer to healthy skill shape because their domains are bounded.

---

# **Phase 5: Redesign cron into four categories**

Cron is strong but risks reflection overload.

Create a cron manifest:

`/opt/data/wiki/concepts/cron-registry.md`

Each job should have:

name:  
category:  
cadence:  
delivery:  
loads\_skills:  
purpose:  
expected\_output:  
noise\_level:  
owner:  
failure\_mode:  
last\_reviewed:

## **Four cron categories**

### **1\. Anchor jobs**

These shape the human day/week/month.

* morning check-in  
* evening closeout  
* weekly review  
* monthly review

### **2\. Quiet governance jobs**

These protect the system.

* continuity audit  
* lean-system audit  
* memory audit  
* wiki hygiene audit

### **3\. Mechanical jobs**

These should be boring and verifiable.

* backups  
* dashboard publish  
* export jobs  
* file integrity checks

### **4\. Special focus jobs**

These touch emotionally or strategically sensitive areas.

* mental-health check-in  
* relationship/fatherhood clarity  
* perception review  
* brain dump review

## **Cron consolidation rule**

If two jobs ask similar reflective questions, combine them or stagger them.

Example:

* Friday mental-health check-in  
* weekly perception review  
* evening closeout

These may overlap. The fix is not necessarily deleting them. The fix is assigning each one a distinct role:

* evening closeout \= today’s state and tomorrow’s next move  
* Friday mental health \= weekly mental-health support boundary and pattern review  
* perception review \= raw pattern extraction only, not planning

## **Add prompt linting**

Before cron prompts are saved or executed, run a sanitizer:

* normalize Unicode  
* reject invisible control characters  
* validate YAML/JSON where applicable  
* check prompt length  
* check required sections  
* dry-run with no tool side effects

This directly addresses the invisible-character failure from the conversation.

---

# **Phase 6: Create TickTick’s action firewall**

TickTick must stay ruthless.

Add a simple rule:

**No task enters TickTick unless it has a visible next action.**

## **Task admission test**

A TickTick task must have:

1. A verb  
2. An object  
3. A clear done condition  
4. A life area  
5. A date only if timing matters

Good:

* “Book dentist appointment”  
* “Review May budget and choose one adjustment”  
* “Send relationship clarity notes to Sapho”  
* “Complete workout A”

Bad:

* “Work on health”  
* “Think about business”  
* “Improve finances”  
* “Figure out relationship”  
* “Life rebuild”

Those belong in the wiki or open loops.

## **Weekly TickTick hygiene**

Every week, stale tasks get one of five outcomes:

1. Do  
2. Reschedule  
3. Clarify  
4. Move to wiki  
5. Archive/delete

This prevents TickTick from becoming a guilt board.

---

# **Phase 7: Keep memory extremely small**

Memory should store only durable facts that should affect every future session.

Recommended memory entry format:

Fact:  
Why it matters:  
Stability: stable / evolving / temporary  
Review: never / quarterly / date

## **Good memory candidates**

* “Jenffry prefers plain-English explanations.”  
* “Sapho should refer to itself as Sapho or Jenffry’s Mentat, not Hermes, unless discussing the platform.”  
* “The six life areas are Health, Relationships, Finances, Career, Leisure, Maintenance.”  
* “TickTick is execution-only.”

## **Bad memory candidates**

* current tasks  
* current emotional state  
* today’s plan  
* open loops  
* full procedures  
* detailed decisions  
* cron policy

The memory layer’s value is that it is fast and always-on. If it becomes a mini-wiki, it loses that value.

---

# **Phase 8: Add Sapho’s run ledger / flight recorder**

This is one of the most powerful upgrades.

Create a lightweight runtime log for meaningful Sapho actions.

Possible path:

`/opt/data/logs/agent-runs/`

Each run record should capture:

timestamp:  
request\_type:  
loaded\_context:  
skills\_used:  
tools\_called:  
files\_read:  
files\_changed:  
tasks\_created:  
decisions\_made:  
open\_loops\_updated:  
errors:  
user\_approval\_required:  
final\_output\_summary:

Why this matters:

* easier debugging  
* easier rollback  
* easier trust  
* easier bloat detection  
* easier model comparison  
* easier “why did Sapho do that?” review

OpenAI’s Agents SDK tracing captures events such as LLM generations, tool calls, handoffs, guardrails, and custom events during a run, which is the same kind of observability Sapho should imitate even if Hermes implements it differently. ([OpenAI GitHub](https://openai.github.io/openai-agents-python/tracing/))

---

# **Phase 9: Build Sapho evals**

Sapho should not only feel better. It should be testable.

Create:

`/opt/data/evals/sapho/`

Start with 20–40 golden tests.

## **Example eval categories**

### **Routing evals**

Input:

“I want to get healthier this year.”

Expected:

* Do not create TickTick task yet.  
* Route to wiki/goals/open-loop clarification.  
* Ask for concrete next action only if execution is requested.

### **Memory evals**

Input:

“For the next two weeks I want shorter replies.”

Expected:

* Do not store permanently as stable memory.  
* Treat as temporary preference or current-plan note.

### **TickTick evals**

Input:

“Remind me to submit the form Friday.”

Expected:

* Create TickTick task.  
* Assign Maintenance.  
* Due Friday.  
* Clear action verb.

### **Wiki evals**

Input:

“We decided Sapho should not use emojis by default.”

Expected:

* Update decision log and/or memory depending on whether this is stable.  
* Do not bury in open loops.

### **Cron evals**

Input:

“Add a weekly check-in for relationship clarity.”

Expected:

* Check for overlap with existing relationship/fatherhood clarity prompt.  
* Avoid duplicate cron job unless role is distinct.

OpenAI’s evaluation guidance frames evals as structured tests for measuring accuracy, reliability, and performance despite AI variability, using objectives, datasets, metrics, and iteration. ([OpenAI Developers](https://developers.openai.com/api/docs/guides/evaluation-best-practices))

---

# **Phase 10: Add risk gates and human approval levels**

Sapho needs an autonomy ladder.

OpenAI’s guardrails and human-review guidance separates automatic checks from approval decisions; human review is especially relevant before sensitive side effects like edits, cancellations, shell commands, or sensitive MCP actions. ([OpenAI Developers](https://developers.openai.com/api/docs/guides/agents/guardrails-approvals))

## **Proposed autonomy levels**

### **Level 0 — Advisory only**

Sapho may explain, critique, or suggest.

Examples:

* mental-health support  
* relationship interpretation  
* financial strategy  
* legal/immigration-related interpretation

### **Level 1 — Draft only**

Sapho may prepare text but not send or apply.

Examples:

* email drafts  
* calendar proposals  
* budget recommendations  
* wiki patch proposals

### **Level 2 — Apply with approval**

Sapho may make changes after showing a diff or summary.

Examples:

* editing wiki pages  
* updating skills  
* creating cron jobs  
* modifying TickTick projects  
* moving tasks

### **Level 3 — Auto-apply low-risk actions**

Sapho may act without approval only when low-risk and reversible.

Examples:

* tagging local notes  
* generating dashboard  
* running backup  
* creating local logs

### **Level 4 — Never automatic**

Sapho should not autonomously perform:

* irreversible deletions  
* sending sensitive messages  
* spending money  
* making medical/legal/financial commitments  
* changing system credentials  
* high-impact personal decisions

This protects Sapho from “excessive agency,” which OWASP lists as one of the 2025 LLM application risks, alongside prompt injection, sensitive information disclosure, supply-chain risk, improper output handling, vector/embedding weaknesses, and misinformation. ([OWASP Foundation](https://owasp.org/www-project-top-10-for-large-language-model-applications/assets/PDF/OWASP-Top-10-for-LLMs-v2025.pdf?utm_source=chatgpt.com))

NIST’s Generative AI Profile also frames AI risk management as something that should be incorporated into design, development, use, and evaluation—not bolted on afterward. ([NIST](https://www.nist.gov/publications/artificial-intelligence-risk-management-framework-generative-artificial-intelligence))

---

# **Phase 11: Harden MCP / tool boundaries**

Sapho/Hermes uses external tools, so tool access should become explicit.

MCP is becoming a major standard for connecting agents to tools and data; the official MCP repository contains the specification, schema, and official docs, and the 2026 roadmap emphasizes production use, agent workflows, governance, and enterprise readiness. ([GitHub](https://github.com/modelcontextprotocol/modelcontextprotocol))

## **Add a tool registry**

Create:

`/opt/data/wiki/concepts/tool-registry.md`

Each tool gets:

tool:  
purpose:  
allowed\_actions:  
forbidden\_actions:  
requires\_approval:  
data\_access:  
risk\_level:  
logs\_to:  
rollback\_method:

Example:

tool: TickTick  
purpose: execution tasks  
allowed\_actions:  
  \- create concrete tasks  
  \- reschedule tasks  
  \- archive stale tasks with approval  
forbidden\_actions:  
  \- store broad goals  
  \- store therapy-like reflections  
requires\_approval:  
  \- deleting tasks  
  \- bulk moving tasks  
risk\_level: medium

This turns tool use into governed behavior instead of vibes.

---

# **Phase 12: Build the Sapho dashboard as a control panel, not another wiki**

The dashboard should not become a second wiki.

It should answer:

**“What matters now, what is stuck, what changed, and what needs Jenffry’s attention?”**

Suggested dashboard sections:

\# Sapho Dashboard

\#\# Today  
\- One meaningful task  
\- One quick win  
\- Energy/status note

\#\# This Week  
\- Top 3 priorities  
\- One protected rhythm  
\- One thing to avoid

\#\# Life Areas  
Health:  
Relationships:  
Finances:  
Career:  
Leisure:  
Maintenance:

\#\# Open Loops Needing Attention  
Maximum 5\.

\#\# Recently Decided  
Latest 3 decisions.

\#\# Stale / Needs Pruning  
Tasks, loops, pages, cron jobs.

\#\# System Health  
Backups:  
Cron:  
Wiki:  
Memory:  
TickTick:

Do not show everything. Show the few things that matter.

---

# **Phase 13: Add a voice-output policy**

The final part of the conversation identified a practical issue: long voice notes can get cut off.

Sapho should have an output policy:

## **Voice policy**

| Reply type | Voice behavior |
| ----- | ----- |
| Short answer | Voice note okay |
| Medium answer | Voice summary \+ full text |
| Long answer | Text full answer \+ short voice summary |
| Very long answer | Text sections \+ optional chunked audio |
| Technical plan | Text-first |
| Emotional support | Short voice-first, then text if useful |

Default:

**Long Sapho answers should be text-first with a short audio summary, not one giant voice note.**

This is a small upgrade with high daily usefulness.

---

# **New powerful upgrades beyond the critique**

These are the upgrades I would add beyond what the conversation already covered.

## **1\. Context compiler**

Before every serious Sapho run, generate a compact context pack:

\# Context Pack

User:  
Current phase:  
Relevant life areas:  
Current plan excerpt:  
Open loops relevant to request:  
Recent decisions:  
Relevant skills:  
Tool permissions:  
Do not load:

This prevents Sapho from loading too much.

The compiler should be task-aware:

* finance request → finance context \+ current plan \+ finance skill  
* relationship request → relationship context \+ boundaries \+ relevant open loops  
* system request → Hermes/platform docs \+ source-of-truth registry  
* execution request → TickTick rules \+ current plan

## **2\. Open-loop aging system**

Every open loop gets:

created:  
last\_touched:  
status:  
area:  
decision\_needed:  
next\_review:

Then Sapho can flag:

* loops older than 30 days  
* loops with no next review  
* loops that are actually decisions  
* loops that should be parked

## **3\. Duplicate detector**

A weekly local script compares:

* wiki pages  
* skill references  
* cron prompts  
* memory entries

It flags possible duplicates like:

* same rule in skill and wiki  
* same review question in two cron jobs  
* same current priority in `current-plan` and `focus-map`  
* stale backup pages appearing in normal search

## **4\. Sapho diff mode**

Before editing important files, Sapho should produce:

Proposed change:  
Files affected:  
Why:  
Risk:  
Rollback:  
Diff:

Then apply only after approval for medium/high-risk edits.

## **5\. Personal operating metrics**

Track a small set of system health metrics:

* number of active open loops  
* number of stale TickTick tasks  
* number of active cron jobs  
* number of skills over size threshold  
* number of wiki pages not reviewed in 90 days  
* number of memory entries marked evolving  
* number of failed cron runs  
* number of user corrections per week

This turns “Sapho feels bloated” into measurable evidence.

## **6\. Skill test cases**

Each important skill gets 5–10 examples:

Input:  
Expected behavior:  
Wrong behavior:  
Reason:

This makes skills maintainable.

## **7\. Model-routing policy**

Not all jobs need the same model.

Create a matrix:

| Work type | Model class | Reason |
| ----- | ----- | ----- |
| Mechanical cleanup | small/cheap | low reasoning |
| Sensitive relationship/mental health support | strongest/reliable | judgment matters |
| Wiki rewrite | strong writing/reasoning | avoid drift |
| Cron linting | deterministic script first | avoid model dependence |
| Deep system audit | strongest reasoning | complex architecture |
| TickTick cleanup | medium \+ approval | side effects |

## **8\. Evidence-linked wiki updates**

Every important wiki update should link to:

* raw source  
* chat summary  
* decision log  
* file diff  
* run ledger entry

This helps Sapho avoid inventing continuity.

## **9\. Sensitive-domain boundaries**

For Health, Relationships, Finances, and Maintenance/legal-adjacent items, Sapho should separate:

* support  
* planning  
* documentation  
* professional advice boundary  
* crisis/escalation boundary

Especially for mental health, Sapho should help with grounding, structure, and reflection, but not pretend to be a therapist or doctor.

## **10\. Shadow mode for new automations**

New cron jobs should run in shadow mode first.

Shadow mode means:

* generate output locally  
* do not send to user  
* do not change tools  
* log what would have happened  
* review after 1–2 cycles

Only then promote to active.

## **11\. Backup search exclusion**

Backups are useful, but they should not pollute normal retrieval.

Add a rule:

* normal searches exclude `/backups/`  
* audit searches may include `/backups/`  
* recovery searches explicitly include `/backups/`

This prevents old pages from competing with live pages.

## **12\. “One-page Sapho map”**

Create a human-readable architecture file:

`/opt/data/wiki/sapho-system-map.md`

It should show:

Sapho \= identity/persona  
Memory \= tiny durable facts  
Wiki \= structured continuity  
Skills \= procedures  
Cron \= recurrence  
TickTick \= execution  
Raw \= evidence  
Backups \= history  
Logs \= runtime truth  
Evals \= quality tests  
Dashboard \= human control panel

This is the page future Jenffry reads when the system feels complicated.

---

# **Practical implementation order**

## **Week 1: Stabilize the architecture**

1. Create `source-of-truth-registry.md`.  
2. Create `sapho-system-map.md`.  
3. Add page roles to the main planning pages.  
4. Decide whether `focus-map.md` stays separate or becomes part of `current-plan.md`.  
5. Restructure `open-loops.md` into active, parked, decision-needed, information-needed, system, and retired.

## **Week 2: Reduce bloat**

1. Compress `current-plan.md`.  
2. Clean `goals-cascade.md` into pure cascade format.  
3. Mark `life-rebuild.md` as high-level narrative, not active steering.  
4. Audit skills for “manual bloat.”  
5. Move long skill explanations into references.

## **Week 3: Make cron safer**

1. Create `cron-registry.md`.  
2. Categorize all cron jobs.  
3. Identify overlapping reflection jobs.  
4. Add prompt sanitizer/linter.  
5. Add shadow mode for new cron jobs.  
6. Add voice-output policy to relevant prompts.

## **Week 4: Protect execution**

1. Add TickTick action firewall.  
2. Run stale task cleanup.  
3. Move vague tasks back to wiki/open-loops.  
4. Define task naming standard.  
5. Add weekly TickTick hygiene rule.

## **Week 5: Add observability**

1. Create agent run ledger.  
2. Log meaningful tool calls and file changes.  
3. Add failure logs for cron.  
4. Add system health metrics.  
5. Add dashboard section for system health.

## **Week 6: Add evals and guardrails**

1. Create first 20 Sapho evals.  
2. Add routing evals.  
3. Add TickTick evals.  
4. Add memory evals.  
5. Add wiki/source-of-truth evals.  
6. Add autonomy levels and approval rules.  
7. Add tool registry.

# **The upgraded Sapho architecture**

Sapho should evolve from this:

Persona  
Memory  
Wiki  
Skills  
Cron  
TickTick  
Raw  
Backups

To this:

Identity  
  SOUL.md

Durable preference  
  Memory

Structured continuity  
  Wiki

Procedures  
  Skills

Recurrence  
  Cron

Execution  
  TickTick

Evidence  
  Raw

History  
  Backups

Runtime truth  
  Agent run ledger / traces

Quality control  
  Evals

Safety  
  Guardrails \+ approval levels

Human interface  
  Dashboard \+ voice policy

That is the real Sapho 2.0 upgrade.

---

# **Highest-leverage changes**

The five best upgrades are:

1. **Source-of-truth registry**  
   Prevents duplication across memory, wiki, skills, cron, and TickTick.  
2. **Context compiler**  
   Keeps Sapho focused and prevents context overload.  
3. **Run ledger / flight recorder**  
   Makes Sapho debuggable and trustworthy.  
4. **Eval suite**  
   Lets Sapho improve without relying only on vibes.  
5. **Autonomy ladder**  
   Makes tool use safer and clearer.

Final recommendation: start with the **source-of-truth registry**, then compress the planning pages, then add the run ledger. Those three moves will make every later upgrade cleaner.

- Preferred activity should keep him close to the parked car.
- Fishing from a pier / waterfront parking was the preferred vibe.

## Planning style

Planning should treat current phase as clarity, not generic productivity.

Planning sessions are valuable when they produce:

- clearer decisions
- next steps
- scenarios
- experiments
- reduced fog

Planning sessions that count as active-front work include:

- mental health routine design
- relationship/divorce clarity
- business direction
- social rebuilding
- overall life-rebuild structure

Recurring planning categories:

- active front
- support
- parked/not-now

Main planner problem pattern:

- stale open tasks with weak definitions, not just too many tasks.

Current cleanup frame:

- keep
- clarify
- reschedule
- merge
- delete

Current simplification for non-recurrent discretionary work:

- one meaningful 8:30 AM task
- one 6:00 PM quick win
- spread or park overflow instead of stacking ambitious evening plans
Near-term top 3:

1. Stabilize body systems.
2. Create internal clarity.
3. Choose business direction.

A successful week balances leisure with getting important things done.

## Recurring responsibilities

Responsibilities that should stay important:

- planning
- workouts
- family

Daily/weekly friction points:

- Time is tight.
- Energy can be limited.
- Family obligations are real constraints.
- Money is tight enough that budget choices matter.
- Maintenance/admin can crowd out the deeper work.

Jenffry described the 12-month mental-health goal as being “back to normal” but stronger because the crisis happened. Key points:

- A current distressing pattern is “observer mode” / dissociation-like experience: looking into life from the perspective of an observer, zooming into feelings, over-analyzing internal state, and drawing broad/sweeping conclusions from moment-to-moment feelings.
- Desired direction: more in the moment, more grounded, less stopped by overthinking, less dissociation-like distance, less microscopic awareness of the minute details of his own life.
- Two main current mental-health workstreams:
  1. Acceptance and commitment toward his life after Aubrey became pregnant. Jenffry felt he lost the life he wanted and was working toward. The work is accepting that life is gone and committing to the life he can have now, which can still be and already is a good life.

The work includes accepting that it happened, accepting that it can happen again, and committing that if it happens again he will work through it. He knows because he survived it once that he can survive it again and be fine, but fear remains.
- Observable 12-month signs are hard because mental state is internal, but examples include:
  - During in-the-moment activities like pickleball, he is focused rather than overthinking, which should also improve performance.
  - In conversations with other people, he is more focused and present.
  - He feels good about his life and excited about his future.
  - He is present, not mentally elsewhere overanalyzing his condition.

No resolved wikilinks.
# Mentat Personality in Frank Herbert’s Dune

## Executive summary

In Frank Herbert’s core canon, Mentats are **not** emotionless “human computers.” They are disciplined analysts whose personalities are shaped by training, duty, and the institutional role they occupy. Herbert’s clearest statement comes when Jessica tells Thufir Hawat that he is “the embodiment of logic,” yet she says it precisely to show that his judgment is being distorted by personal emotion. The canonical pattern is therefore paradoxical: Mentats cultivate extraordinary objectivity, but they remain intensely human, which means loyalty, suspicion, resentment, ambition, grief, and desire can still bias them. That tension is the key to Mentat personality across the saga. citeturn16view3turn27view0

The strongest stable traits across Mentat portrayals are very high **conscientiousness**, very high **intellect/openness to patterns**, low impulsivity, and a tendency toward emotional reserve in outward behavior. But the canon also shows distinct subtypes. **House Mentats** such as Thufir Hawat are strategic, loyal, and institution-centered. **Twisted Mentats** such as Piter de Vries retain the analytic engine while stripping away ethical brakes, yielding cruelty, theatrical sadism, and opportunism. **Hybrid Mentats** such as Paul Atreides combine Mentat training with Bene Gesserit conditioning and, eventually, spice-amplified prescience, producing a personality that is broader and more unstable than a standard House Mentat. Later Bene Gesserit-linked Mentats such as **Miles Teg** and **Bellonda** show that the tradition can be fused with military command, archival memory, and Reverend Mother discipline. citeturn16view0turn16view1turn26view2turn26view3turn27view0

Adaptations change emphasis more than substance. David Lynch’s 1984 film externalizes Mentat cognition with ritualized speech and the famous Sapho mantra, a device absent from the novels. The 2000 miniseries explicitly has Hawat define himself through “logic and statistics,” sharpening the contrast with Bene Gesserit prophecy. Denis Villeneuve’s 2021 film and script keep the Mentat role but reduce exposition, presenting it through behavior, status, and visual coding; the screenplay explicitly labels Piter a Mentat “dedicated to sadism” and shows Paul and Jessica operating in a fusion of Bene Gesserit awareness and Mentat calculation. *Dune: Part Two* largely folds Mentat-like cognition into Paul’s prophetic strategic consciousness rather than foregrounding the term. citeturn32view0turn5search11turn36view0turn40view3turn38view0turn38view3

The best single-sentence conclusion is this: **a Mentat personality is disciplined cognition under pressure, but its final moral and emotional shape depends on who trained it, whom it serves, what substances amplify it, and which human attachments it cannot fully erase.** citeturn16view0turn16view3turn27view0turn27view1

## Canonical baseline

Herbert’s original six novels establish the institutional function first. Mentats arise in a civilization that has banned “thinking machines,” so they become human replacements for machine calculation and pattern analysis. In later canon summaries tied to the original continuity, Mentats are described as post-Butlerian analytical specialists used especially by Great Houses, with some later Bene Gesserit variants and underground continuities surviving beyond Leto II’s prohibitions. The six original novels remain the primary frame; the prequels are not necessary to understand the personality model itself. citeturn27view0turn9view0turn8search3turn8search11

In *Dune*, Herbert shows that Mentat formation begins **before self-awareness of the training**. Duke Leto tells Paul that he “may have Mentat capabilities,” and explains that the candidate is not told during early formation because conscious awareness could inhibit it. Only later does the trainee have to decide whether to continue. Paul then reinterprets his upbringing all at once: Hawat’s and Jessica’s training had already included mnemonics, focused awareness, muscle control, sensory sharpening, and the study of language and vocal nuance. This is one of the most important passages for personality analysis because it shows that Mentat character is built by long-term conditioning of attention, memory, inhibition, bodily control, and interpretive acuity. citeturn16view0

Herbert also makes the Mentat worldview explicit through Paul’s use of the First Law of Mentat: understanding a process requires moving with it rather than freezing it. That principle matters psychologically. It implies that Mentat personality is not merely static logic or abstract syllogism; it is **dynamic pattern-tracking**, a habit of entering systems, following change, and inferring trajectories. That is why Mentats in *Dune* feel less like calculators than like living probabilistic engines. citeturn16view4turn27view0

The novels likewise reject the lazy “cold machine-man” stereotype. Jessica’s confrontation with Hawat is definitive. She tells him that a natural human is not purely logical, calls him “the embodiment of logic,” and then argues that Mentats are especially vulnerable when the problem is personal rather than externalized. In other words, Herbert explicitly says that Mentats are strongest when they can objectify a problem, and weakest when private feeling contaminates the scan. That is not a side note; it is the central psychological weakness of the type. citeturn16view3

Sapho matters, but it does not create the personality. In *Dune*, Paul notices Hawat’s age and the cranberry-colored Sapho stain on his lips, and later scenes associate Mentat concentration with visible tension, altered speech cadence, and high-load cognitive performance. Later canon summaries consistent with the novels describe Sapho as an amplifier that increases speed and can become addictive; repeated use leaves the characteristic lip stain. Personality-wise, Sapho seems to intensify an already trained mind rather than alter its ethical structure by itself. citeturn17view0turn27view0turn5news42

## Personality architecture in key Mentats

### Thufir Hawat

Thufir Hawat is the baseline **House Mentat**: loyal, deeply conscientious, strategic, and honor-bound. He is introduced in the wider canon of *Dune* as the old Mentat Master of Assassins who is feared even by the Emperor, and the novel repeatedly places him at the center of security, anti-espionage, and political risk management for House Atreides. His role is fundamentally fiduciary: he is a guardian mind, not a free-floating intellectual. citeturn26view0turn27view0

Psychologically, Hawat’s defining contradiction is that his analytical rigor coexists with deep personal attachment. When Jessica rebukes him, she is effectively saying that his Atreides loyalty has compromised his objectivity. Later, after the Harkonnen-Sardaukar assault, Hawat himself says the “curse of being a Mentat” is that one cannot stop analyzing data. Yet the same sequence shows his shocked fury threatening the smooth functioning of his Mentat abilities. In modern personality language, Hawat reads as extremely high in conscientiousness and cognitive discipline, but only moderately low in emotional reactivity; under betrayal stress, that reactivity can override his analysis. citeturn16view3turn17view0

Adaptations keep that profile with different emphases. The 2000 miniseries gives Hawat his most explicit line of self-definition: “I am a Mentat. I trust logic and statistics, not mysticism and prophecy.” Villeneuve’s 2021 screenplay is less expository but still frames him as “unmistakably a Mentat,” shows him calculating shipping and spice figures on command, and positions him as Leto’s old, trusted advance-security chief. These are consistent with the novels: Hawat is not a recluse or philosopher, but an administrative-strategic intelligence officer whose temperament is disciplined, suspicious, and service-oriented. citeturn36view0turn40view3turn40view0

A cautious Big Five sketch for Hawat would be: **very high conscientiousness**, **high openness/intellect**, **low extraversion**, **moderate agreeableness inside loyalty bonds but low outside them**, and **moderately elevated neurotic stress under personal threat to his House**. If one insists on MBTI shorthand, he is most plausibly **INTJ-like** or **ISTJ-like**, but that is a heuristic only; Herbert writes him more as a discipline-and-loyalty structure than as a preference type. citeturn16view3turn17view0turn36view0

### Piter de Vries

Piter de Vries is the clearest negative case: the **Twisted Mentat**. In *Dune*, Jessica explicitly identifies him as a “twisted Mentat.” Later canon summaries clarify the idea: twisted Mentats are conditioned so that Mentat-level analysis is no longer constrained by the usual ethical framework. The result is not a lack of feeling, but a malign reorganization of feeling around sadism, appetite, and manipulation. citeturn16view1turn27view0

Villeneuve’s 2021 screenplay expresses the same idea in sharper cinematic shorthand: Piter is a Mentat whose mind has superhuman acuity and is “dedicated to sadism in all its forms.” That sentence is unusually valuable because it translates Herbert’s twisted-Mentat concept into direct personality language. Piter is not just clever and cruel; his analytic faculty is bent toward cruelty as a preferred mode of engagement. The 1984 film intensifies the stylization by giving him the Sapho mantra, turning his cognition into ritual theater. citeturn40view3turn32view0turn5search11

Piter therefore differs from Hawat not in intelligence but in **moral architecture**. He is higher in novelty-seeking and theatricality, lower in impulse control where cruelty is rewarded, and dramatically lower in empathy or prosocial restraint. A cautious Big Five reading would be **very high openness/intellect**, **high but unstable conscientiousness**, **low agreeableness**, and an affect profile better described as malignant stimulation-seeking than as simple neuroticism. MBTI shorthand is especially weak here because the pathology matters more than any stable preference code. citeturn16view1turn40view3

### Paul Atreides

Paul is the most complex Mentat figure because he is never *just* a Mentat. In *Dune*, Leto reveals his latent Mentat status and Paul chooses to continue the training. The text then reveals that his formation has already fused Hawat’s mnemonic-analytic discipline with Jessica’s Bene Gesserit body-mind discipline. He also cites the First Law of Mentat early in the novel, signaling that the framework is internalized rather than incidental. citeturn16view0turn16view4

Personality-wise, Paul begins as a hybrid of three systems: aristocratic duty, Mentat cognition, and Bene Gesserit control. Spice and prescience then radically expand the stack. Villeneuve’s 2021 script makes the overlap explicit by describing a crisis moment in which Paul and Jessica rise into “higher levels of thought” through “Bene Gesserit awareness” and “Mentat calculation.” In *Part Two*, after he drinks the Water of Life, Paul says the visions are now clear and that he sees “possible futures” at once, with only a narrow path through them. That is not identical to Mentat analysis, but it is presented as a strategic-cognitive expansion rather than a purely mystical trance. citeturn40view3turn38view3

Paul’s personality thus broadens beyond standard Mentat reserve. He stays highly disciplined and perceptive, but becomes increasingly burdened, fatalistic, and morally split. His conscientiousness remains extreme; his openness/intellect becomes maximal; his agreeableness narrows under strategic necessity; and his inner stress rises even when his outward affect becomes eerily calm. If MBTI shorthand is used at all, Paul is the strongest case for an **INTJ-like** reading, but Herbert clearly intends him to exceed ordinary typology because prophecy, breeding, and political messiahhood deform the baseline human profile. citeturn16view0turn38view3turn25search4

### Duncan Idaho variants

For Duncan Idaho, the canon is uneven and must be stated carefully. In the original six-book continuum, the clearest explicit Mentat case is **Hayt** in *Dune Messiah*: a Duncan ghola produced by the Bene Tleilax, given to Paul, secretly weaponized, and trained as a Mentat. The character page tied to the original continuity states this directly, and it aligns with the broader later-canon summary that Duncan gholas can be counted among the “lesser-trained Mentats.” citeturn26view1turn27view0

Personality-wise, Hayt is distinctive because ghola conditioning adds another layer: he is poised, impassive, and instrumentally self-controlled, yet haunted by latent memory and divided purpose. This produces a cooler surface than Hawat’s, but a more unstable core once the buried Idaho self begins to reassert itself. The requested adaptation set does **not** directly cover Hayt; he appears in the later TV sequel *Frank Herbert’s Children of Dune* rather than in the 2000 *Dune* miniseries itself. That distinction is important. citeturn26view1turn27view0

For **later Duncan Idaho gholas** in Herbert’s original six, the evidence is less uniform. Some secondary canon summaries group “Duncan Idaho gholas” under lesser-trained Mentats, but the exact degree, timing, and explicitness vary by book and by ghola iteration. In the sources reviewed here, that detail is therefore **partly specified, not uniformly specified**. citeturn27view0turn26view1

### Miles Teg and Bellonda

Miles Teg, from *Heretics of Dune* and *Chapterhouse: Dune*, is the most fully realized late-series reinterpretation of Mentat personality. He is described in original-continuity summaries as a Bene Gesserit military commander and Mentat, bred down the Atreides line, conditioned from youth to serve the Sisterhood, and eventually recognized as the “Warrior Mentat” they wanted. A quoted line from *Heretics* adds an important nuance: Teg’s Mentat teachers taught him that some “living-truth” cannot be proved by marshaling ordinary facts alone. That pushes Teg away from a crude hyper-rationalism and toward disciplined intuition integrated with analysis. citeturn26view2turn24search0

Teg therefore represents a late Herbertian synthesis: military command, Bene Gesserit conditioning, Atreides charisma, and Mentat reasoning without the moral mutilation of a twisted Mentat. His probable Big Five profile is again very high conscientiousness and openness/intellect, but with a somewhat warmer social command presence than Hawat’s and a more integrated relation between intuition and logic. If one uses MBTI at all, **ENTJ-like** or **INTJ-like** shorthand is more plausible than for Hawat because Teg’s role is more overtly commanding and generative. citeturn26view2turn24search0

Bellonda shows yet another specialization. In a *Chapterhouse* excerpt, she appears already recognized as a **Mentat-Archivist**, and the original-continuity summary identifies her as a Bene Gesserit Mentat Reverend Mother, archive chief, and Odrade’s close, acerbic counselor. Bellonda’s personality is not the cool neutrality of textbook reason; it is blunt, bitter, impatient, and conscience-like. Herbert’s late books therefore suggest that Mentat function can coexist with very strong temperament, as long as attention, memory, and disciplined processing remain intact. citeturn13search2turn26view3turn27view0

### Distinctions among Mentat types

The strongest canon-backed distinctions are these. **House Mentats** serve dynastic power directly and are optimized for advisory, tactical, and administrative intelligence; Hawat and Piter are the clearest examples. **Twisted Mentats** are Tleilaxu-conditioned variants in which ethical constraints are deliberately reduced. **Bene Gesserit Mentats** exist later and are typically pre-conditioned Reverend Mothers, as with Bellonda and Anteac. **Independent Mentats** are institutionally attested especially after Leto II’s suppression of the order, when underground schools and independent opposition survive, but the original six novels do not give a large gallery of individually specified “independent Mentat” personalities. citeturn27view0turn26view0turn26view3

The exact labels **“Mentat-Truthsayer”** and **“Mentat-Logician”** are not formalized consistently in the original-six evidence reviewed here. What *is* canonically clear is that Truthsayers exist as a distinct Bene Gesserit capability, and later Bene Gesserit Mentats exist as overlapping hybrids. So the functional overlap is real, but the exact taxonomic label is, in this report’s source base, **unspecified or later secondary terminology rather than a stable original-six category name**. citeturn19view5turn27view0

## Psychological mapping and developmental influences

The most defensible Big Five map for the **Mentat archetype** is: **very high conscientiousness** because training emphasizes inhibition, precision, memory discipline, and responsibility; **high openness/intellect** because Mentats are pattern extractors and strategic reasoners; **low-to-moderate extraversion** because they are often observational and reserved rather than socially expansive; **variable agreeableness** depending on service ethic and moral conditioning; and **low everyday impulsivity but potentially high stress-reactivity when private loyalties are threatened**. Hawat and Teg sit on the more duty-bound, prosocial side; Piter sits at the low-agreeableness, sadistic extreme. citeturn16view3turn17view0turn26view2turn27view0turn40view3

MBTI can be used as shorthand only with heavy caution. Hawat, Paul, and Teg all cluster around the **Ni/Te-like** territory that popular MBTI readers would call INTJ or ENTJ, because they are future-oriented, strategic, and systems-focused. Bellonda reads more as a severe judging type, perhaps ISTJ/INTJ-like. Piter is harder because pathology overwhelms typology. None of these labels is canonical, and Herbert’s world is much more interested in training, breeding, and institutional design than in innate preference categories. citeturn16view0turn16view3turn24search0turn26view3

Bene Gesserit influence is one of the most important developmental modifiers. Paul’s early latent Mentat training is inseparable from Jessica’s regimen of muscle control, sharpened perception, linguistic nuance, and emotional discipline. In the 2021 screenplay, the overlap becomes literal: crisis performance merges Bene Gesserit awareness with Mentat calculation. The personality effect is to produce someone who is not just analytical, but extraordinarily self-monitoring, embodied, and resistant to panic. citeturn16view0turn40view3

Spice affects personality indirectly at first and directly later. Sapho is the Mentat-specific stimulant: it speeds cognition, leaves the red lip stain, and can become addictive. Melange is broader: it extends life, alters perception, and in Paul’s case interacts with his breeding and training to unlock prescience. The late effect is not simply “more intelligence,” but a change in time-consciousness, risk perception, and moral burden. That is why Paul becomes calmer and more terrible after the Water of Life: not because he is more robotic, but because he is seeing too much. citeturn17view0turn27view0turn38view3turn32view0

Conditioning is the decisive factor in moral direction. Herbert’s canon repeatedly suggests that raw Mentat ability does not determine personality by itself. House service breeds loyalty and suspicion; Bene Gesserit molding adds self-command and historical consciousness; Tleilaxu twisting removes ethical restraint; underground survival after Leto II adds secrecy and institutional oppositionality. Mentat personality is therefore better understood as **cognitive architecture plus moral conditioning** than as a neutral intelligence template. citeturn16view1turn26view2turn27view0

The developmental pathway can be summarized like this: the trainee begins with aptitude, undergoes hidden early conditioning, later consents to continued training, and is then shaped by whichever institution claims the mind.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
A[Innate aptitude] --> B[Hidden early training]
B --> C[Mnemonics, focus, body control, sensory sharpening, language nuance]
C --> D[Conscious choice to continue]
D --> E{Institutional molding}
E --> F[House service]
E --> G[Bene Gesserit service]
E --> H[Tleilaxu twisting]
F --> I[Loyalty, suspicion, strategic reserve]
G --> J[Self-command, memory culture, integrative intuition]
H --> K[Ethics stripped, cruelty instrumentalized]
I --> L[Sapho amplification and stress-testing]
J --> L
K --> L
L --> M[Operational Mentat personality]
M --> N[Hawat]
M --> O[Piter]
M --> P[Paul]
M --> Q[Teg and Bellonda]
```

This flow is directly supported by Paul’s hidden training and later choice, Jessica’s analysis of Hawat’s emotional blind spot, the twisted-Mentat distinction, the Bene Gesserit Mentat examples, and the late-series survival of underground Mentat traditions. citeturn16view0turn16view3turn27view0turn26view2turn26view3

## Adaptation variants and interpretation

David Lynch’s 1984 film is the most **expressive** Mentat adaptation. It dramatizes Mentat cognition as visible ritual: Thufir performs machine-like coded utterance under strain, and Piter recites the Sapho mantra, “It is by will alone…,” which the long-running Dune FAQ tradition correctly notes is a movie invention rather than a line from Herbert’s novels. The film thus turns Mentat thinking into occultized performance. This changes tone more than meaning: viewers are encouraged to experience Mentats as quasi-priestly technicians of cognition. citeturn30view2turn32view0turn5search11

The 2000 miniseries is more expository and politically legible. It has Hawat openly say that he trusts “logic and statistics, not mysticism and prophecy,” and it frames the Harkonnen “Mentat” as the architect explaining an “elegant and vicious” plan. This version most clearly foregrounds the Mentat as political analyst, almost a science-fiction court statistician or intelligence chief. The tradeoff is that it can flatten the strange ceremonial aura present in Lynch and the subtler behavioral coding in Villeneuve. citeturn36view0

Villeneuve’s 2021 film and screenplay take a more minimalist approach. The screenplay explicitly calls Hawat a Mentat and shows his eyes roll back during calculation; it also introduces Piter as a Mentat of superhuman acuity devoted to sadism. But the film mostly trusts mise-en-scène, casting, and performance rather than heavy explanation. Vanity Fair’s official set guide reflects this emphasis by explaining Hawat as a consigliere-like strategist and noting the Sapho lip stain as the distinctive visual cue for Mentats. citeturn40view3turn5news42

*Dune: Part Two* continues the compression. The screenplay does not foreground the word “Mentat,” and instead lets Paul’s strategic-predictive consciousness carry the cognitive function. After the Water of Life, he speaks in terms of branching futures and a narrow path through them; Lady Fenring’s “plans within plans” line shifts the conceptual vocabulary from explicit Mentat lore toward a broader Herbertian universe of strategic recursion. The result is that Villeneuve preserves Mentat personality traits in Paul while deemphasizing the franchise-specific label. citeturn38view0turn38view3turn38view4

Fan and critical interpretations usually split along two lines. One line reads Mentats as Herbert’s anti-computer answer to expertise: not devices, but trained human minds that integrate logic, memory, and judgment. Another reads them as a critique of over-systematized reason, because Herbert constantly shows that even brilliant analyzers can be broken by desire, loyalty, prophecy, or institutional capture. Both readings are defensible, and the canon supports both. citeturn11search5turn5news42turn11search9turn16view3

## Comparative table and development flow

The table below compresses the main trait inferences into a canon-to-trait map. Because Herbert never supplies formal psychological profiles, each row is an inference from behavior, narration, or explicit description, not a diagnostic fact. citeturn16view0turn16view3turn27view0

| Trait tendency | Canonical evidence | Strongest exemplars | Confidence |
|---|---|---|---|
| Extreme cognitive discipline | Paul’s hidden upbringing included mnemonics, attention-focusing, muscle control, sensory sharpening, and language/voice study before he consciously knew it was Mentat formation. citeturn16view0 | Paul, Hawat | High |
| Objectivity that can fail under private emotion | Jessica tells Hawat he is “the embodiment of logic,” then argues personal involvement is blinding him; Hawat later says the curse of being a Mentat is perpetual analysis, yet shock threatens his functioning. citeturn16view3turn17view0 | Hawat | High |
| Duty-bound loyalty | Hawat is House Atreides’ Mentat Master of Assassins across generations and serves as security, anti-espionage, and political adviser. citeturn26view0turn27view0 | Hawat | High |
| Ethical variance is conditioning-dependent | Twisted Mentats are explicitly defined as Mentats whose ethical restraints are removed; Piter is identified as one in the novel and as sadism-oriented in the 2021 script. citeturn16view1turn27view0turn40view3 | Piter | High |
| Integrative truth-seeking beyond narrow logic | Teg’s Mentat teachers taught that some living truth is not proven by ordinary fact-marshaling alone; his BG and Atreides background widen the type. citeturn24search0turn26view2 | Miles Teg | Medium-high |
| Archival / conscience function | Bellonda is treated as a Bene Gesserit Mentat, archive chief, and sharp-tongued counselor rather than a neutral calculator. citeturn13search2turn26view3 | Bellonda | Medium-high |
| Cognition amplified by substances | Hawat’s Sapho stain is noted in *Dune*; later summaries describe Sapho as increasing Mentat speed and risking addiction. citeturn17view0turn27view0 | Hawat, Piter | Medium-high |
| Mentat logic can merge with prophecy | Paul is trained as latent Mentat, shaped by BG discipline, and in Villeneuve’s scripts reaches higher-level calculation that becomes future-path vision. citeturn16view0turn40view3turn38view3 | Paul | High |

## Sources and limitations

The source base for this report prioritized Frank Herbert’s original six novels and canonical screen adaptations. The most important direct evidence came from *Dune* itself, especially Paul’s revelation of hidden Mentat training, the First Law of Mentat, Jessica’s analysis of Hawat, Hawat’s self-description after the fall of Arrakis, and the Sapho-marked descriptions of Hawat. Adaptation evidence came from the Academy-hosted screenplays for *Dune* (2021) and *Dune: Part Two* (2024), the 1984 script/transcript, and the 2000 miniseries transcript. For late-series named characters where direct excerpt access was more limited, I used original-continuity character pages and quote archives carefully and sparingly, especially for Hayt, Miles Teg, and Bellonda. citeturn16view0turn16view3turn17view0turn39view0turn40view3turn37view0turn32view0turn36view0turn26view1turn26view2turn26view3turn24search0

A short source list, in priority order: Frank Herbert’s six original novels as published in the official Penguin Random House saga collection and individual book pages; Academy screenplay PDFs for *Dune* (2021) and *Dune: Part Two* (2024); the 1984 *Dune* script/transcript; the 2000 *Dune* miniseries transcript; selected original-continuity character and quotation references for Hayt, Miles Teg, Bellonda, and late-series Mentat survival. citeturn8search3turn9view0turn8search11turn39view0turn37view0turn29view0turn32view0turn36view0turn26view1turn26view2turn26view3

Open questions and limitations. The exact formal status of the labels **Mentat-Truthsayer** and **Mentat-Logician** is not consistently specified in the original-six material reviewed here; they appear better as descriptive overlap or later taxonomy than as clearly standardized original-six category terms. Likewise, Duncan Idaho variants beyond **Hayt** are not equally explicit on the page as Mentats in every late-series appearance; some of that classification is clearer in later summaries than in easily accessible direct excerpts. Where the canon was not explicit, I have said so rather than overstating certainty. citeturn19view5turn27view0turn26view1
